Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning in Zina
Lists conditions and provides proofs for stoning the muhsan adulterer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan required for stoning (rajm) according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence for each condition from the proof chain provided.

Core Idea
Ihsan for stoning requires five conditions: freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, and a valid consummated marriage with a similarly qualified spouse.

Stoning (rajm) is the prescribed punishment for a married adulterer, but not every married adulterer qualifies. The Hanafi school stipulates that the offender must be 'muhsan'—a status that depends on a specific set of conditions. This lesson examines those conditions and the evidence the classical scholars used to establish them, drawing on the matn of al-Quduri and the subsequent commentary that marshals proofs from the Quran, hadith, and statements of early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
First, recognize that the passage deals with the hadd punishment for zina. The default punishment is 100 lashes (Quran 24:2), but stoning is a more severe punishment limited to those who meet the conditions of ihsan. The matn lists five conditions: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and having consummated a valid marriage with both spouses in that state.
The conditions are cumulative—all must be present for stoning to apply.
2
Examine the Proofs for Freedom
Proofs 1 and 2 address the condition of freedom. The hadith of the slave-girl (Proof 1) states that a slave is only flogged, not stoned. The Quranic verse (Proof 2) says that slave women receive half the punishment of free women, implying full punishment (stoning) only for free persons.
These proofs establish that slaves are categorically excluded from stoning.
3
Examine the Proofs for Adulthood and Sanity
Proofs 3 and 4 use hadiths about the lifting of the pen from minors and the insane, and the Prophet's question to a man about madness. These show that only adults of sound mind are liable for the full hadd punishment.
Adulthood is defined as puberty; sanity is presumed unless proven otherwise.
4
Examine the Proof for Islam
Proof 5 (the story of the Jewish couple) might seem to suggest that non-Muslims can be stoned, but the Hanafi interpretation is that they were stoned under their own law, not as muhsan Muslims. Proof 6 (Ibn Umar's statement) and Proof 7 (Ibn Mas'ud's hadith) are used to argue that only Muslims can be muhsan. This is the point of cross-madhhab discussion.
The Hanafi school requires the offender to be Muslim; a non-Muslim married fornicator receives lashes, not stoning.
5
Examine the Proof for Valid Marriage and Consummation
Proofs 9 and 10 from Ata emphasize that actual intercourse is necessary for ihsan; a marriage without consummation does not make one muhsan. Proof 8 mentions lashes for a non-muhsan, reinforcing the distinction.
Both spouses must be in the state of ihsan at the time of marriage and consummation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَشَرْطُ إِحْصَانِ الرَّجْمِ أَنْ يَكُونَ حُرًّا بَالِغَا عَاقِلًا مُسْلِمًا قَدْ تَزَوَّجَ امْرَأَةَ نِكَاحًا صَحِيحًا وَدَخَلَ بِمَا وَهُمَا عَلَى صِفَةِ الْإِحْصَانِ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَهُ يَقُولُ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا زَنَتِ الأَمَةُ فَتَبَيَّنَ زِنَاهَا، فَلْيَجْلِدْهَا وَلَا يُقَرِّبْ ثُمَّ إِنْ زَنَتْ فَلْيَجْلِدْهَا وَلَا يُقربْ ثُمَّ إِنْ زَنَتِ الثَّالِثَةَ فَلْيَبِعْهَا وَلَوْ بِحَبْلِ مِنْ شَعَرِ» (صحيح البخاري)
وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت: وَفَإِنْ أَتَيْنَ بِفَاحِشَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ (سورة النساء، 25)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت: عن علي، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ: عَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ، وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ، وَعَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ حَتَّى يَعْقِلَ» (سنن أبي داود)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت: دَعَاهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: «أَبِكَ جُنُونٌ؟» قَالَ: «لَا» (صحيح البخاري)
وجه (۵) الحديث لثبوت: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «أُتِيَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَهُودِي وَيَهُودِيَّةٍ قَدْ أَحْدَثَا جَمِيعًا، فَقَالَ لَهُمْ: مَا تَجِدُونَ فِي كِتَابِكُمْ؟ قَالُوا: إِنَّ أَحْبَارَنَا أَحْدَثُوا تَحْمِيمَ الْوَجْهِ وَالتَّجْبِيةَ، قَالَ عَبْدُ اللهِ بْنُ سَلَام: ادْعُهُمْ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ بِالتَّوْرَاةِ، فَأْتِي بِهَا، فَوَضَعَ أَحَدُهُمْ يَدَهُ عَلَى آيَةِ الرَّجْمِ، وَجَعَلَ يَقْرَأُ مَا قَبْلَهَا وَمَا بَعْدَهَا، فَقَالَ لَهُ ابْنُ سَلَامٍ: ارْفَعْ يَدَكَ، فَإِذَا آيَةُ الرَّجْمِ تَحْتَ يَدِهِ، فَأَمَرَ بِهِمَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَرْجِمَا، قَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: فَرْجِمَا عِنْدَ الْبَلَاطِ» (صحيح البخاري ومسلم)
وجه (۶) دليل الشافعى قول الصحابي: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: «مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنٍ» (الدارقطني)
وجه (۷) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا يَحِلُّ دَمُ امْرِئٍ مُسْلِمٍ، يَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَأَنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ، إِلَّا بِإِحْدَى ثَلَاثٍ: الثَّيِّبُ الزَّانِي، وَالنَّفْسُ بِالنَّفْسِ، وَالتَّارِكُ لِدِينِهِ الْمُفَارِقُ لِلْجَمَاعَةِ» (صحيح مسلم)
وجه (۸) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ... «وَعَلَى ابْنِكَ جَلْدُ مِائَةٍ، وَتَغْرِيبُ عَامٍ» (صحيح مسلم)
وجه (۹) قول التابعى: عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ تَزَوَّجَ بِامْرَأَةٍ، ثُمَّ دَخَلَ بِمَا فَإِذَا أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ، قَالَ: «لَيْسَ بِإِحْصَانٍ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق)
وجه (۱۰) قول التابعى: عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ: «الْإِحْصَانُ أَنْ يُجَامِعَهَا، لَيْسَ دُونَ ذَلِكَ إِحْصَانٌ، وَلَا يُرْجَمُ حَتَّى يَشْهَدُوا لَرَأَيْنَاهُ يُغَيِّبُ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنْهَا» (مصنف عبدالرزاق)
اصول: باب زنا میں اگر زانیہ محصن ہوں ہو تو رجم کیا جائے گا، اور غیر محصن کو سو کوڑے مارے جائیں گے۔ اصول : محصن ہونے شرائط: امسلمان، ۲ آزاد، ۳ عاقل، بالغ، ۴ نکاح صحیحہ کیا ہو ،۵ اپنی منکوحہ سے وطی کی ہو اس حال میں کہ دونوں محصن ہو۔
And the condition of ihsan for stoning is that he be free, adult, sane, Muslim, that he married a woman with a valid marriage and consummated it, while both are in the state of ihsan. Evidence (1): Hadith from Abu Hurayrah: 'When a slave-girl commits adultery and her adultery is proven, then flog her and do not rebuke...' (Bukhari). Evidence (2): Quran: '...then upon them half of what is upon the muhsanat of the punishment' (4:25). Evidence (3): Hadith from Ali: 'The pen is lifted from three: the sleeper, the boy, and the madman' (Abu Dawud). Evidence (4): Hadith: The Prophet asked a man, 'Are you mad?' He said no (Bukhari). Evidence (5): Hadith of Ibn Umar about the Jewish man and woman stoned (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (6): Proof from Shafi'i: saying of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' (Darqutni). Evidence (7): Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The blood of a Muslim is not permissible except by one of three: the married adulterer, life for life, and the apostate' (Muslim). Evidence (8): Hadith from Abu Hurayrah: 'And upon your son is one hundred lashes and banishment for a year' (Muslim). Evidence (9): Saying of Ata regarding a man who married a woman then found she was his foster sister: 'This is not ihsan' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). Evidence (10): Ata said: 'Ihsan is that he has intercourse with her; there is no ihsan without that, and he is not stoned until they testify that they saw him insert it into her' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). Principles: In the chapter of zina: if the adulteress is muhsan, she is stoned; if not muhsan, she receives one hundred lashes. Principles: Conditions of ihsan: (1) Muslim, (2) free, (3) sane, adult, (4) valid marriage, (5) intercourse with his wife while both are in the state of ihsan.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage provides the five conditions required for the hadd of stoning (rajm) in cases of adultery. The matn states that the offender must be: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and must have contracted a valid marriage and consummated it with a spouse who also meets these conditions. The commentator then marshals ten proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and early authorities to support each condition. For example, the hadith about the slave-girl (proof 1) shows that slaves are only flogged, not stoned, establishing the free condition. The verse on half-punishment for slave women (proof 2) similarly indicates distinction between free and slave. The hadiths on mental competency (proofs 3 and 4) establish sanity and adulthood. The hadith of Ibn Umar about the Jewish couple (proof 5) shows the necessity of being Muslim (as they were Jews but were stoned under Islamic law, but the condition of Islam for ihsan is derived elsewhere). Proof 6 quotes Ibn Umar's statement that a polytheist is not muhsan, which is used by Imam al-Shafi'i to argue that only Muslims can be muhsan. The Hanafi school accepts this condition. Proof 7 from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud lists the married adulterer as one whose blood is permissible, implying the death penalty only for the thayyib (married) adulterer. Proof 8 mentions lashes and banishment for the non-muhsan. Proofs 9 and 10 from Ata emphasize that actual intercourse is necessary for ihsan; a marriage without consummation does not make one muhsan. The Urdu summary at the end reiterates the conditions in bullet points.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being married and having consummated the marriage with a free, adult, sane, Muslim spouse.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a hadd punishment for a muhsan adulterer.
محصن (muhsan): A person who meets all conditions for rajm: free, adult, sane, Muslim, previously married and consummated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for ihsan that makes stoning applicable?
A) The offender must be free.
B) The offender must have consummated the marriage with a spouse who also meets the conditions.
C) The offender must have married a slave woman who is not Muslim.
D) The offender must be adult and sane.

Key Takeaway
Stoning is only for the muhsan adulterer who meets all five conditions; any missing element reduces the punishment to lashes.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Ta'zir for Intercourse Less than Private Part
Ruling on ta'zir for sexual contact less than zina with a stranger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sexual contact less than full zina and explain why it is ta'zir rather than hadd.

Core Idea
No hadd without full penetration – lesser contact merits ta'zir.

This lesson from al-Quduri's matn addresses an important boundary in the law of hudud. While zina (full intercourse) carries a fixed hadd punishment, any sexual contact that falls short of full penetration does not qualify as zina. The Hanafi school holds that such acts are punishable by ta'zir, a discretionary punishment left to the judge. The ruling is supported by a report from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri regarding the punishment for lesbian acts, which serves as an analogy for non-penetrative sexual offences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
Carefully read the opening statement: 'Whoever has intercourse with a stranger woman in what is below the private part is given ta'zir.' Note that the phrase 'intercourse' (wati') here does not imply full penetration; it is a euphemism for sexual contact short of the private part.
The term 'duna al-farj' is key: it means 'less than the private part', so the act does not meet the Shari'ah definition of zina.
2
Understand Why No Hadd Applies
In Hanafi fiqh, zina is defined as the full insertion of the glans into the vagina or anus. Without that, there is no fixed hadd. Instead, the act is sinful and subject to the judge's discretion (ta'zir).
This distinction is critical to avoid applying hudud punishments where the strict conditions are not met.
3
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The author provides a proof: the statement of Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, who reported that the early scholars prescribed one hundred lashes for women who engage in lesbian rubbing (sahq). This shows that non-penetrative sexual acts are punished by ta'zir, not hadd.
The hadith is mursal (from a Tabi'i), so its thubut is zanni, but it is accepted as evidence in the Hanafi school for establishing ta'zir.
4
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The parallel is clear: if women engaging in sexual contact without penetration receive lashing as ta'zir, then men doing the same with a non-mahram should also receive ta'zir. The punishment amount (100 lashes) is not fixed; the judge can reduce it as ta'zir is discretionary.
This analogy (qiyas) is based on the common factor of sexual contact without full penetration.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Status
The Hanafi position is that only full penetration constitutes zina; other acts are lesser offenses. Some other schools may define zina more broadly (e.g., any contact of circumferences). This difference leads to different punishments for the same act, which is a practical consequence.
You may recall that the Shafi'i school requires imprisonment for zina, but the definitional difference remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٣ وَمَنْ وَطِئَ أَجْنَبِيَّةً فِيمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ عُزّرَ
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ أَجْنَبِيَّةً فِيمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ عُزِّرَ \ أَخْبَرَنِي ابْنُ شِهَابٍ قَالَ: «أَدْرَكْتُ عُلَمَاءَنَا يَقُولُونَ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ تَأْتِي الْمَرْأَةَ بِالرَّفْغَةِ وَأَشْبَاهِهَا، تُجْلَدَانِ مِائَةٌ مِائَةً، الْفَاعِلَةُ وَالْمَفْعُولَةُ بِهَا » ) » مصنف عبد الرزاق ، بَابُ السَّحَاقَةِ، نمبر 13383)
33. And whoever has intercourse with a stranger in what is below the private part (i.e., less than full penetration) is given ta'zir. Proof: The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: And whoever has intercourse with a stranger in what is below the private part is given ta'zir: Ibn Shihab informed me, he said: 'I found our scholars saying concerning a woman who approaches a woman with a pad and similar things: both are flogged one hundred lashes each, the active and the passive.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Sahq, no. 13383)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi matn of al-Quduri, followed by a proof (wajh). The ruling states that if a man engages in sexual contact with a stranger woman that is less than full vaginal intercourse (i.e., between the thighs or similar), he is not subject to the hadd punishment for zina but rather receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The proof provided is the statement of Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, a Tabi'i, who reports that the early scholars (ulama) prescribed one hundred lashes for lesbian acts (sahq) as ta'zir. This analogy indicates that any sexual act short of zina does not incur hadd but requires ta'zir.

Key Terms
عُزّرَ (uzzira): He is given ta'zir, a discretionary punishment determined by the judge.
دُونَ الْفَرْجِ (duna al-farj): Less than the private part; meaning any sexual contact that does not involve full vaginal or anal penetration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the punishment for a man who engages in sexual contact with a stranger woman that is less than full intercourse (e.g., between the thighs)?
A) Hadd of 100 lashes
B) Hadd of rajm (stoning)
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment)
D) No punishment at all

Key Takeaway
Sexual contact short of full penetration of the glans does not constitute zina; the offender receives ta'zir at the discretion of the judge.

No Hadd for Intercourse with Son's Slave-girl
Ruling that hadd is not applied for intercourse with one's own son's or grandson's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no hadd applies for intercourse with one's son's slave-girl and explain the role of shubhah in repelling the hadd.

Core Idea
A father's property link creates a legal doubt that repels the hadd punishment.

This lesson examines a unique ruling in Hanafi hudud law: if a man has intercourse with a slave-girl owned by his son or grandson, the fixed punishment for zina is not applied. This is true even if he admits knowledge of the prohibition. The ruling is based on a hadith that establishes a father's special connection to his son's property, which creates a legal doubt (shubhah) sufficient to repel the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first sentence of the matn. What is the act, and what is the legal consequence? The act is intercourse with a son's slave-girl, and the consequence is that no hadd is applied.
Note the phrase 'even if he says: I knew it was forbidden.'
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'You and your property belong to your father...' Identify which type of proof this is (Sunnah ahad).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? It implies that the father has a right over the son's property, creating a doubt about the exclusive ownership of the slave-girl. This doubt (shubhah) is the basis for dropping the hadd.
Hanafi usul: hudud are repelled by shubuhat.
4
Evaluate the Scope and Ikhtilaf
Does this ruling apply if the father knew it was forbidden? Yes, the matn explicitly says so. Is there disagreement? Some schools may not accept this shubhah and would apply hadd if knowledge is admitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۵ وَلَا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ وَلَدِهِ أَوْ وَلَدِ وَلَدِهِ وَإِنْ قَالَ عَلِمْت أَنَّهَا حَرَامٌ
۳۵ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ وَلَدِهِ \ أَنْتَ وَمَالُكَ لِوَالِدِكَ، إِنَّ أَوْلَادَكُمْ مِنْ أَطْيَبِ كَسْبِكُمْ، فَكُلُوا مِنْ كَسْبِ أَوْلَادِكُمْ، سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَأْكُلُ مِنْ مَالِ وَلَدِهِ، نمبر 3530)
35. And there is no hadd upon whoever has intercourse with the slave-girl of his son or the slave-girl of his grandson, even if he says: I knew it was forbidden. 35. Proof: The hadith for establishing no hadd upon whoever has intercourse with the slave-girl of his son: 'You and your property belong to your father; indeed your children are among the best of your earnings, so eat from the earnings of your children.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on a man eating from his son's wealth, no. 3530)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This is a ruling statement followed by its proof. The matn states that if a man has intercourse with a slave-girl owned by his son or grandson, the hadd punishment for zina is not applied, even if he admits knowledge that it was forbidden (i.e., he knew she was not his own property). The justification is based on the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father,' which indicates a type of ownership right of the father over the son's property. This creates a legal doubt (shubhah) regarding the ownership of the slave-girl, and doubts (shubuhat) are sufficient to repel the fixed punishments (hudud) in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
حَدَّ (hadd): The fixed punishment for zina; here it is dropped due to shubhah.
شُبْهَة (shubhah): A legal doubt that exists in the mind of the perpetrator regarding the permissibility of the act. This particular shubhah is mālī (financial) due to the father's connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a father not receive the hadd punishment for intercourse with his son's slave-girl, even if he knew it was forbidden?
A) Because the slave-girl is not a free woman
B) Because the father has no liability for his son's property
C) Because the son's property is considered like the father's due to the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father'
D) Because the act is not zina

Key Takeaway
A father's connection to his son's property creates a legal doubt that repels the hadd punishment, even if he knew the act was forbidden.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Hadd for Intercourse with Father's or Mother's Slave-girl
Ruling on when hadd is applied for intercourse with certain relatives' slave-girls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when hadd is applied for intercourse with a relative's slave-girl and explain how a claim of mistaken belief drops the punishment.

Core Idea
A claim of mistaken belief in permissibility drops the hadd; admission of knowledge confirms it.

This passage deals with a sensitive area of criminal law: intercourse with slave-girls owned by close relatives. The Hanafi school, drawing on prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions, establishes a crucial distinction between knowingly committing a prohibited act and acting under a genuine but mistaken belief. The ruling protects individuals from severe punishment when there is room for doubt, embodying the principle that hudud are repelled by shubuhat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
First, recognize that intercourse with a slave-girl not owned by the man or not made lawful to him is generally zina (forbidden) and subject to hadd. The passage specifically addresses slave-girls of father, mother, wife, and master.
2
Distinguish between the two claims
The ruling pivots on the perpetrator's statement: if he says 'I knew it was forbidden' (علمت أنها حرام), the hadd is applied. If he says 'I thought it was permissible' (ظننت أنها تحل لي), no hadd is applied.
The claim must be plausible; a bare assertion without any basis may not suffice.
3
Understand the legal basis (shubhah)
The hadd is dropped because of shubhah (doubt). The claim of mistaken belief creates a doubt about the criminal intent, and hudud are set aside in cases of doubt.
The hadith about the wife's slave-girl shows that permission (from the wife) reduces the punishment; by extension, a perceived permission (like thinking it was allowed) creates a similar doubt.
4
Note the implication for the accuser (qadhf)
If the actor is not liable for hadd, then a person who accuses him of zina (qadhf) also does not receive hadd for slander, because the act is not proven to be zina.
This prevents double injustice.
5
Compare the evidence from the Salaf
The third proof shows a difference among early scholars: Hammad and al-Hakam said hadd applies, al-Hasan said no hadd. The Hanafi ruling adopts the view of al-Hasan and reinforces it with the hadith and athar.
This ikhtilaf shows the issue was not settled among the Salaf, and the Hanafi school chose the more lenient position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٦ وَإِذَا وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَبِيهِ أَوْ أُمِّهِ أَوْ زَوْجَتِهِ أَوْ وَطِئَ الْعَبْدُ جَارِيَةَ مَوْلَاهُ فَإِنْ قَالَ: عَلِمْت أَنَّهَا حَرَامٌ حُدَّ وَإِنْ قَالَ: ظَنَنْت أَنَّهَا تَحِلُّ لِي فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا عَلَى قَاذِفِهِ أَيْضًا
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَبِيهِ أَوْ أُمِّهِ \ عَنِ النُّعْمَانِ بْنِ بَشِيرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَأْتِي جَارِيَةَ امْرَأَتِهِ، قَالَ: " إِنْ كَانَتْ أَحَلَّتْهَا لَهُ جَلْدُ مِائَةٍ، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ أَحَلَّتْهَا لَهُ رَجَمْتُهُ، (سنن بیهقی، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَتَى جَارِيَةَ امْرَأَتِهِ ، غمبر 17068)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَبِيهِ أَوْ أُمِّهِ اوَعَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، أَنَّ عَلِيًّا قَالَ: «حَسْبُهُم مِنَ الْفِتْنَةِ أَنْ يُنْفَوْا، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ النَّفْيِ،نمبر 13320)
وجه : (۳) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَبِيهِ أَوْ أُمِّهِ اسألت حمادا والحكم عن الرجل يقع على جارية ،أمه، قالا: عليه الحد، وعن الحسن قال : ليس عليه حد،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الرجل يأتي جارية أمه ،مبر 30477)
36. And when someone has intercourse with the slave-girl of his father, or his mother, or his wife, or a slave has intercourse with his master's slave-girl: if he says 'I knew it was forbidden', he is hadded; and if he says 'I thought it was permissible for me', then there is no hadd upon him, and also no hadd on his slanderer (qadhif). Proof (1): The hadith for establishing: when he has intercourse with the slave-girl of his father or his mother: from al-Nu'man b. Bashir from the Prophet that he said concerning a man who has intercourse with his wife's slave-girl: 'If she had made her lawful for him, then flogging of one hundred; if she had not made her lawful for him, then I would stone him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab...no. 17068). Proof (2): from Ibrahim that Ali said: 'Sufficient for them from the fitnah is that they be expelled.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Nafi, no. 13320). Proof (3): The saying of the Tabi'i: I asked Hammad and al-Hakam about a man who has intercourse with his mother's slave-girl; they both said: upon him is hadd; and from al-Hasan: no hadd upon him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 30477)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This ruling addresses several cases of intercourse with slave-girls owned by certain relatives or masters. The key principle is that the application of hadd depends on whether the perpetrator knew of the prohibition or had a mistaken belief of permissibility. If he says 'I knew it was forbidden,' then hadd applies because no doubt exists. If he says 'I thought it was permissible for me' (i.e., due to some misconception like assuming a right of ownership), then hadd is dropped due to shubhah. From the proofs: the hadith about the wife's slave-girl shows that if the wife makes her lawful, it is not zina but incurs a lesser punishment (flogging); if she does not, it is full zina deserving rajm. The athar from Ali about expulsion (nifā') indicates that in cases of doubt, a lesser punishment suffices. The third proof shows disagreement among the Salaf: Hammad and al-Hakam impose hadd, while al-Hasan does not. The Hanafi ruling combines these: the application of hadd depends on the claim of knowledge or doubt.

Key Terms
قَاذِفِهِ (qādhifihi): The slanderer of the person who committed the act. The ruling says that if the actor is not liable for hadd, then the one who slanders him (by accusing him of zina) also does not receive hadd for qadhf, because the act is not proven to be zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this ruling, when is the hadd punishment applied for intercourse with a father's slave-girl?
A) Always, regardless of the perpetrator's claim
B) Only if the perpetrator says 'I thought it was permissible'
C) Only if the perpetrator says 'I knew it was forbidden'
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The application of hadd for intercourse with a relative's slave-girl hinges on the perpetrator's claim: admission of knowledge triggers it; a plausible claim of mistaken belief drops it.

Hadd for Intercourse with Brother's or Uncle's Slave-girl
Ruling that hadd applies if a man claims mistaken belief of permissibility for brother's or uncle's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man claims mistaken belief of permissibility for his brother's or uncle's slave-girl and evaluate whether the claim drops the hadd.

Core Idea
A claim of mistaken belief is not accepted as a valid shubhah if there is no legal basis — hadd applies.

This ruling contrasts with the previous case of a father's slave-girl, where a claim of mistaken belief could drop the hadd due to potential ownership or inheritance rights. Here, for a brother or uncle, no such right exists, so the claim is rejected. The proofs from al-Zuhri and Umar establish that the hadd is not waived by a mere subjective belief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the claim
The act is intercourse with the slave-girl of a brother or uncle. The man claims 'I thought she was permissible for me.' This claim is a claim of shubhah (doubt).
2
State the ruling
The matn says 'he is hadded.' The hadd is applied despite the claim. The ruling is that the claim does not create a valid shubhah.
3
Examine the first proof
From al-Zuhri: A man who fornicated with his wife's slave-girl is flogged, not stoned. This shows that when there is some connection (marriage) the punishment is reduced to ta'zir, but here no such connection exists.
The flogging here may be hadd (100 lashes) or ta'zir, but it indicates a punishment is applied.
4
Examine the second proof
From Umar: A similar case was raised to him, and he flogged the man 100 lashes without stoning. No mention of accepting a shubhah claim.
Umar's action sets a precedent that the hadd is enforced.
5
Understand the principle
The Urdu asool states: 'The hadd is dropped due to doubt of ownership.' But here there is no doubt, because a brother or uncle has no ownership claim over each other's property.
Valid shubhah requires an objective legal basis, e.g., inheritance or purchase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَخِيهِ أَوْ عَمِهِ، وَقَالَ ظَنَنْت أَنَّهَا تَحِلُّ لِي حُدَّ
۳۷وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِيَ جَارِيَةَ أَخِيهِ أَوْ عَمِهِ اعَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ زَلَى بِوَلِيدَةِ امْرَأَتِهِ قَالَ: «يُجْلَدُ، وَلَا يُرْجَمُ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُصِيبُ وَلِيدَةَ امْرَأَتِهِ ، نمبر 13431)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ جَارِيَةَ أَخِيهِ أَوْ عَمِهِ \ قَالَ: رُفِعَ أَمْرُهُ إِلَى عُمَرَ أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فَجَلَدَهُ مِائَةً، وَلَمْ يَرْجُمْهُ فَقَالَ: لَا أَعْلَمُهَ إِلَّا قَالَ: فَسَأَلَ الْمُصَّدَّقُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَوَجَدَهُ كَمَا أَخْبَرَهُ الرَّجُلُ " . مصنف عبد الرزاق ، بَابُ الرَّجُل يُصِيبُ وَلِيدَةَ امْرَأَتِهِ، نمبر 13430)
اصول: ملکیت کی شبہ سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
And whoever has intercourse with the slave-girl of his brother or his uncle and says: I thought she was permissible for me, is hadded. 37. Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: someone who fornicates with his wife's little slave-girl: al-Zuhri said: 'He is flogged and not stoned.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Rajul yusibu walidata imraatihi, no. 13431). Proof (2): The saying of the Sahabi for establishing: the matter was raised to Umar, the Commander of the Faithful, and he flogged him one hundred and did not stone him; he said: I do not know except that he said: so the honest man asked about that and found it as the man had informed him. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Rajul yusibu walidata imraatihi, no. 13430). Principle: The hadd is dropped due to doubt of ownership (milk).
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This ruling contrasts with the previous one. In the case of a brother's or uncle's slave-girl, even if the man claims he thought it was permissible (due to some misconception of ownership), he is still subject to hadd. The proofs indicate that the earlier scholars (al-Zuhri) said he is flogged but not stoned, and Umar flogged a man in a similar case but did not stone him. This shows that the claim of shubhah is not accepted for these relatives, because the relationship does not create any ownership right. The Urdu asool at the end explains the general principle: 'The hadd is dropped due to doubt of ownership.' However, in this case, no such doubt exists because a brother or uncle has no claim over each other's property, so the shubhah is invalid.

Key Terms
ظَنَنْت (zanantu): I thought, I assumed (a mistaken belief). In this context, the claim is not accepted as a valid shubhah.
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt or ambiguity that can mitigate the hadd punishment. Must be based on a recognized legal right in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ta'zir only
C) Hadd of flogging (100 lashes)
D) Hadd of stoning

Key Takeaway
A claim of mistaken belief does not automatically drop the hadd; it must be based on a plausible legal right, such as ownership or marriage.

No Hadd for Mistaken Marriage (Bride Switched)
Ruling on mistaken intercourse due to false identification as wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man unknowingly has intercourse with a woman mistakenly presented as his bride, and explain the role of shubhah in repelling hadd.

Core Idea
Shubhah (doubt) from a credible claim of marriage repels the hadd for zina, but the mahr is still due.

Imagine a wedding night where the bride presented is not the man's actual wife, but the attending women assure him she is. If he consummates the marriage, is he guilty of zina? The Hanafi school rules that the hadd punishment is dropped because of the doubt created by the women's assertion. However, since the marriage was not valid, he must compensate the woman with her mahr. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its proof from the early generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is sexual intercourse with a woman who is not one's wife. Normally, this would be zina and incur the hadd punishment. Note the default condition.
Zina requires full awareness and absence of any marital claim.
2
Recognize the shubhah (doubt) that changes the ruling
The women's statement that she is his wife creates a reasonable belief in the man's mind. This doubt removes the element of knowing transgression required for hadd.
Shubhah can arise from a claim, a defective contract, or an honest mistake.
3
Understand the consequence: no hadd, but mahr wajib
Because hadd is repelled by shubhah, the man is not punished. However, since intercourse occurred without a valid marriage, the woman is entitled to her mahr as compensation for her person.
The mahr is wajib (obligatory) in Hanafi fiqh for any intercourse under a semblance of marriage.
4
Examine the proof from the Tabi'i Ibrahim
Ibrahim's statement: 'If this were true, no hadd would be upon the fornicator' shows that a woman's claim of marriage is sufficient to create shubhah and drop the hadd, even if the claim might be false.
The proof is from a Tabi'i (qawl al-tabi'i), which is considered a valid source in Hanafi usul for such rulings.
5
Trace the practical application (thamarah al-khilaf)
The ruling applies to any scenario where a man has intercourse under a credible but false belief that the woman is his wife. The hadd is always repelled, but financial restitution is required.
This differs from schools that might require ta'zir if the man was negligent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ زُفَّتْ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرَ امْرَأَتِهِ، وَقَالَتْ النِّسَاءُ : إِنَّهَا زَوْجَتُك فَوَطِئَهَا فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْمَهْرُ
۳۸ وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ زُفَّتْ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرَ امْرَأَتِهِ \ ويحيى بن أبي الهيثم عن جده أنه شهد عليا وأتي برجل وامرأة وجدا في خرب مراد، فأتي بهما علي فقال: بنت عمي (يتيمتي) في حجري، فجعل أصحابه يقولون: قولي زوجي، فقالت: هو زوجي، فقال علي: خذ بيد امرأتك، عن إبراهيم في المرأة (توجد) مع الرجل فتقول: (تزوجني)، فقال إبراهيم: (لو) كان هذا حقا ما كان على زان حد، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الرجل يوجد مع المرأة فتقول: زوجي ، غمر 30815)
وجه: (ا) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ زُفَّتْ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرَ امْرَأَتِهِ \ عن إبراهيم في المرأة (توجد) مع الرجل فتقول: (تزوجني)، فقال إبراهيم: (لو) كان هذا حقا ما كان على زان حد،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الرجل يوجد مع المرأة فتقول: زوجي ،نمر 30815)
And whoever has a woman other than his wife presented (as a bride) to him, and the women say: 'She is your wife,' and he has intercourse with her, then there is no hadd upon him, and he must pay the mahr. 38. Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i: Yahya b. Abi al-Haytham from his grandfather that he witnessed Ali when a man and woman were brought who were found in a ruin (khirb) of Murad; Ali brought them and said: 'My cousin (my orphan) is in my lap'; his companions began saying: 'Say: my husband'; she said: 'He is my husband'; then Ali said: 'Take your wife's hand.' From Ibrahim concerning a woman found with a man who says: 'He married me'; Ibrahim said: 'If this were true, no hadd would be upon the fornicator.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 30815).
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where a man is presented with a woman who is not his wife, but the women present claim she is his wife. If he then has intercourse with her, no hadd is imposed because he has a reasonable belief (shubhah) that she is his wife, based on the women's testimony. However, he must pay the mahr (dower) to the woman because a valid marriage did not actually occur, so he has used her for physical pleasure without proper contract. The proofs from Ali and Ibrahim show that when a woman claims to be a man's wife, the man is not guilty of zina, and no hadd is applied. The principle is that the presence of a contractual-like situation creates a shubhah that repels the hadd.

Key Terms
زُفَّتْ (zuffat): Presented as a bride; led to the groom's home for the wedding night.
الْمَهْر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift that must be paid to the woman because intercourse took place under a semblance of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must pay the mahr to the woman
C) He must compensate the woman's guardian
D) He must pay the mahr only if she was a virgin

Key Takeaway
A credible claim of marriage creates a shubhah that repels the hadd for zina, but the mahr is wajib as compensation for the woman.

6 min
No Hadd Due to Shubha, but Mahr Is Due
Ruling on a man deceived into intercourse with a woman not his wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man who is deceived into intercourse with a woman presented as his wife, and explain why no hadd is imposed and mahr is wajib.

Core Idea
Shubha removes hadd, but mahr remains obligatory because intercourse occurred.

This lesson presents a case from al-Quduri's matn on hudud: a man who mistakenly believes a woman is his wife and has intercourse. The Hanafi school rules that the fixed penalty (hadd) is dropped due to the doubt (shubha) created by the circumstances, but the man must still pay the mahr. We will examine the ruling and the proof from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The man is deceived: a woman is brought to him as a bride, women confirm she is his wife, and he has intercourse. This creates a reasonable doubt about the legality of the act.
The doubt arises from external factors (the women’s claim), not from the man’s own assumption.
2
State the ruling
No hadd is imposed. The man must pay the mahr (dower) to the woman.
The ruling has two parts: dropping of punishment and financial obligation.
3
Understand the rationale
The presence of shubha (doubt) removes the fixed penalty for zinā because the essential condition for hadd—knowledge that the act is unlawful—is missing.
Shubha does not make the intercourse halal; it only averts the criminal penalty.
4
Analyse the proof
The proof is a statement from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a prominent tābi'ī. He said, 'If this were true, there would be no hadd on a fornicator.' This shows that a claim of marriage, even if false, creates enough doubt to negate hadd.
The proof is a qawl of a tābi'ī, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
5
Connect to the ruling
Ibrahim’s statement is applied analogically: if a mere claim of marriage removes hadd in one case, then in this case, with stronger evidence (the women confirming), the hadd is also removed.
The man had actual belief based on testimony, so the doubt is even stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ زُفَّتْ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرَ امْرَأَتِهِ، وَقَالَتْ النِّسَاءُ : إِنَّهَا زَوْجَتُك فَوَطِئَهَا فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْمَهْرُ. وَجْهُ الدَّلِيلِ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ (تُوجَدُ) مَعَ الرَّجُلِ فَتَقُولُ: (تَزَوَّجَنِي)، فَقَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ: (لَو) كَانَ هَذَا حَقًّا مَا كَانَ عَلَى زَانٍ حَدٌّ.
And whoever has a woman brought to him as a bride who is not his wife, and the women say: She is your wife, and he has intercourse with her, then there is no hadd upon him, and he owes the mahr. The face of the proof: From Ibrahim regarding a woman who is found with a man and she says: He married me, so Ibrahim said: If this were true, there would be no hadd on a fornicator.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri on hadd penalties. The case involves a man who is deceived into believing a woman is his wife—she is brought to him as a bride and the women of the family confirm it. He then has intercourse. According to the Hanafi school, no hadd (fixed penaly for zinā) is imposed because his action is based on a mistaken belief (shubha) that she is lawful. However, he must pay the proper mahr because intercourse has occurred with a woman to whom he is not married. The proof comes from a statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a prominent tābi'ī, who reasoned that if such a claim is true, the man would not be a fornicator deserving hadd. This shows the principle that shubha removes hadd.

Key Terms
زُفَّتْ (zufifat): Brought as a bride to the groom's house
الْمَهْرُ (al-mahr): The bridal gift (dower) that becomes obligatory upon marriage or intercourse

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a woman brought to a man as his wife but she is not, what is the ruling on hadd according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hadd is required because intercourse occurred outside marriage.
B) No hadd because of shubha (doubt), but mahr is due.
C) No hadd and no mahr because he was deceived.
D) Hadd is reduced to ta'zir.

Key Takeaway
Shubha removes the fixed penalty for zinā, but the obligation of mahr remains because the act of intercourse itself is not excused.

No Shubha for the Man Who Finds a Woman in His Bed
Ruling on a man who finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a man who finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse, and identify the absence of shubha as the key condition for hadd.

Core Idea
Finding a woman on one's bed does not create lawful doubt – hadd is wajib.

This ruling from the Matn of al-Quduri is a clear statement of the Hanafi position on zinā where no shubha (doubt) exists. Unlike earlier cases where a man might be deceived or could plausibly claim a marriage, here the man simply finds an unknown woman on his bed. The Hanafi school holds that mere presence does not constitute a valid excuse; the man must verify before intercourse. Therefore, the full hadd penalty applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text describes a man who finds a woman on his bed (firāshihi) and then intentionally has intercourse with her. There is no mention of any prior relationship, claim, or deception.
The word 'firāsh' simply means his place of sleep – no special legal connotation.
2
Recognize the absence of shubha
In Hanafi fiqh, shubha (doubt) that negates hadd must be based on a plausible legal claim, such as a claim of marriage or a valid contract. Merely finding a woman on one's bed does not create such doubt; the man could have asked or left.
Contrast this with the case of a man who marries a woman without witnesses – there shubha exists.
3
State the ruling and penalty
Since no shubha exists, the act is zinā and the hadd penalty is wajib: stoning if muhsan, otherwise one hundred lashes.
The penalty is the fixed hadd, not ta'zir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَجَدَ امْرَأَةً عَلَى فِرَاشِهِ فَوَطِئَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ
And whoever finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse with her, then upon him is the hadd.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling from the matn. Unlike the previous case where the man was deceived, here a man finds a woman on his bed—presumably he does not know her or she is not his wife—and he intentionally has intercourse. Since there is no shubha (reasonable doubt) about her being lawful, he is guilty of zinā and must receive the full hadd penalty (stoning if muhsan, lashing if not). The Hanafi school does not count mere presence on his bed as sufficient shubha to negate hadd, because the man can verify.

Key Terms
فِرَاشِهِ (firāshihi): His bed (the place of sleep)
الْحَدُّ (al-hadd): The fixed corporal punishment for zinā (flogging or stoning)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the penalty for a man who finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse?
A) No penalty, because he may have assumed she was his wife.
B) He must pay mahr only.
C) He receives the hadd penalty for zinā.
D) He receives ta'zir only.

Key Takeaway
A man who has intercourse with a woman he finds on his bed without any claim of marriage is liable for hadd because no shubha exists.

No Hadd for Marriage with Prohibited Woman
Ruling on marriage with a woman whom it is unlawful to marry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd when a marriage with a permanently prohibited woman is consummated, and explain the basis using the two cited hadiths.

Core Idea
Even an invalid marriage contract creates a shubha that averts the fixed hadd penalty for zinā.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a critical ruling about the interaction between marriage contracts and the severe penalty of hadd. The Hanafi position is that the existence of a formal, though invalid, marriage contract creates enough doubt (shubha) to prevent the application of the zinā hadd. This ruling is grounded in two hadiths that emphasize averting penalties where possible and show that the Prophet did not apply hadd in a similar case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage deals with a person who contracts a marriage that is essentially invalid (e.g., with a mahram) and then has intercourse. The ruling is that the fixed hadd for zinā is not required.
The act is consummation under a void marriage.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: the first from A'ishah instructs to avert hadd as much as possible; the second from Yazid ibn al-Bara' shows that the Prophet sent someone to execute a man who married his father's wife, not to apply zinā hadd.
The second hadith distinguishes between execution and zinā hadd.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith establishes a principle of avoiding hadd when possible. The second demonstrates that the Prophet's punishment for marrying a prohibited woman was execution, not the zinā hadd, proving that the existence of a marriage contract removes the hadd from zinā.
The presence of a contract, even if void, creates shubha.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools like the Shafi'i may differ; they may hold that if the prohibition is clear, no shubha exists, and hadd applies. However, the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered stronger because it adheres strictly to the principle of averting hadd and follows the explicit precedent of the Prophet in the second hadith.
The mufta bihi is 'no hadd'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَزَوَّجَ امْرَأَةً لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ نِكَاحُهَا فَوَطِئَهَا لَمْ يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ. وَجْهُ الدَّلِيلِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ادْرَءُوا الحُدُودَ عَنِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ». (سنن ترمذي، نمبر 1424) وَعَنْ يَزِيدَ بْنِ الْبَرَاءِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: لَقِيتُ عَمّى وَمَعَهُ رَايَةٌ، فَقُلْتُ لَهُ: أَيْنَ تُرِيدُ؟ قَالَ: «بَعَثَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِلَى رَجُل نَكَحَ امْرَأَةَ أَبِيهِ، فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ أَضْرِبَ عُنُقَهُ، وَآخُذَ مَالَهُ». (سنن ابوداود، نمبر 4457)
And whoever marries a woman whose marriage is not lawful for him and has intercourse with her, then hadd is not required upon him. The face of the proof: From A'ishah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hadd penalties from the Muslims as much as you can.' (Tirmidhi no. 1424) And from Yazid ibn al-Bara' from his father who said: I met my uncle with a banner and asked: Where are you going? He said: 'The Messenger of Allah sent me to a man who married his father's wife, and commanded me to strike his neck and take his property.' (Abu Dawood no. 4457)
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This ruling covers cases where a person contracts a marriage that is fundamentally invalid, such as marrying a mahram (e.g., father's wife, mother, sister). Despite the invalidity of the contract, if intercourse occurs, the hadd for zinā is not imposed. Why? Because there is a shubha (doubt) arising from a formal marriage contract. The acted upon the contract, even if defective, creates uncertainty about the ultimate prohibition. The first hadith (dar'u al-hudud) is a general principle to avoid hadd where possible. The second hadith shows that the man who married his father's wife was executed (the Prophet commanded it), but note that this was not hadd for zinā but a separate punishment for violating the sanctity of marriage. In Hanafi law, the man would not receive the zinā hadd but could be subject to ta'zir. This demonstrates that even in severe prohibition, the existence of a contract removes the fixed hadd.

Key Terms
لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ نِكَاحُهَا (lā yahillu lahu nikāḥuhā): Women permanently prohibited in marriage (e.g., mahram)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hadd not imposed on a man who marries a prohibited woman and has intercourse?
A) Because the woman consented.
B) Because the existence of a marriage contract creates shubha.
C) Because the man is ignorant of the prohibition.
D) Because the hadd requires four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
An invalid marriage contract creates a shubha that averts the fixed hadd penalty for zinā.

Liwat: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir – The Hanafi Position
Ruling on liwat with dalil and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the punishment for liwat and explain the interpretive difference with the Sahibayn regarding the hadith.

Core Idea
Liwat carries no fixed hadd in the Hanafi school; the judge imposes ta'zir, which may include execution.

The text from Al-Quduri presents Abu Hanifa's view that anal intercourse and sodomy carry no fixed hadd punishment, only discretionary ta'zir. This lesson unpacks the dispute with the Sahibayn, who analogize liwat to zinā, and explores the proof (dalīl) and its interpretation. Understanding this ikhtilāf reveals how strict textual boundaries define the fixed punishments in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Recognize that the passage discusses two acts: anal intercourse with one's wife (al-mawdiʿ al-makrūh) and sodomy (ʿamal qawm Lūṭ). Both are considered haram but differ in the debate over their punishment.
The act itself is unanimously haram; the dispute focuses on whether it triggers the fixed hadd of zinā or a discretionary taʿzīr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
From the text: 'lā ḥadda ʿalayhi ʿinda Abī Ḥanīfah' – there is no hadd upon him according to Abu Hanifa. Instead, the judge imposes ta'zīr, which can range from admonition to execution.
This is the muftā bihī (operative) position in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the dalīl (proof) cited
The passage quotes the hadith: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lūṭ, kill the active and the passive.' Abu Hanifa interprets this as a prescription for ta'zīr (a discretionary death penalty), not a fixed hadd.
The hadith is used by both sides but interpreted differently.
4
Contrast with the opposing position
The Sahibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī) and several tābiʿūn, including al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī and Ibrāhīm al-Nakhaʿī, hold that liwāṭ carries the same hadd as zinā (stoning for muḥṣan, flogging for non-muḥṣan). They rely on qiyās and the same hadith, reading it as a fixed punishment.
The difference hinges on whether the command to 'kill' is a fixed hadd or a permissible ta'zīr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَتَى امْرَأَةَ فِي الْمَوْضِعِ الْمَكْرُوهِ أَوْ عَمِلَ عَمَلَ قَوْمٍ لُوطٍ فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَجْهُ الدَّلِيلِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ وَجَدْتُمُوهُ يَعْمَلُ عَمَلَ قَوْمٍ لُوطٍ، فَاقْتُلُوا الْفَاعِلَ، وَالْمَفْعُولُ بِهِ». وَقَالَ بَعْضُ أَهْلِ العِلْمِ مِنْ فُقَهَاءِ التَّابِعِينَ مِنْهُمْ : الحَسَنُ البَصْرِيُّ، وَإِبْرَاهِيمُ النَّخَعِيُّ، وَعَطَاءُ بْنُ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ، وَغَيْرُهُمْ، قَالُوا: حَدُّ اللُّوطِيَ حَدُّ الزَّانِي، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الثَّوْرِيِّ، وَأَهْلِ الْكُوفَةِ. أُصُول: كسی نے عورت سے یا مرد سے لواطت کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک حد نہیں ہو گی البتہ تعزیر ہوگی.
And whoever has intercourse with a woman in the disliked place (anus) or commits the act of the people of Lut (sodomy) — there is no hadd upon him according to Abu Hanifa. The face of the proof: From Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lut, kill the active and the passive.' And some of the people of knowledge from the tabi'un, including Hasan al-Basri, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Ata ibn Abi Rabah, and others, said: The hadd of the sodomite is the hadd of the fornicator, and that is the statement of al-Thawri and the people of Kufa. Usul: Whoever commits liwat (sodomy) with a woman or a man, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no hadd; however, there is ta'zir.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage discusses the punishment for anal intercourse (with one's wife) and sodomy (with a male). Abu Hanifa's position is that there is no fixed hadd (either flogging or stoning) for these acts. Instead, the ruler may impose a discretionary punishment (ta'zir), which can even include execution if deemed necessary. The proof cited is the hadith ordering execution of those who engage in sodomy; Abu Hanifa interprets this as ta'zir, not hadd. The opposing view (held by the Sahibayn, al-Thawri, and many tabi'un) is that the sodomite deserves the same hadd as a fornicator (rajm if muhsan, flogging if not). The Hanafi school favors Abu Hanifa's view based on the principle that hadd applies only to zinā defined as vaginal intercourse by a non-married person. Note that the Urdu text confirms: no hadd but ta'zir, and ta'zir can include execution.

Key Terms
الْمَوْضِعِ الْمَكْرُوهِ (al-mawdiʿ al-makrūh): The anal opening; considered disliked because it is unlawful for intercourse
التَّعْزِيرُ (al-taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge, not fixed by Shariah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on the punishment for sodomy (liwat)?
A) The same fixed hadd as zinā (stoning/flogging).
B) No punishment at all; the act is not a legal offense.
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment) only.
D) A mandatory death penalty derived from the hadith.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, liwat carries no fixed hadd; the punishment is discretionary ta'zir, leaving room for judicial assessment.

Bestiality: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir
Ruling with proof for bestiality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and explain how the two seemingly contradictory hadiths are reconciled to derive ta'zir instead of hadd.

Core Idea
Bestiality carries no fixed hadd; the judge imposes ta'zir, even execution.

This lesson addresses a specific offense that falls outside the fixed punishments (hudud) of zinā. The Hanafi school relies on two reports from Ibn Abbas to determine that there is no hadd, but the offender is subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir), which may include death. Understanding this ruling requires careful reconciliation of the apparent conflict between the two hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intercourse with an animal. The Hanafi ruling: no hadd, only ta'zir. The phrase 'فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ' explicitly negates the fixed punishment.
Hadd is the fixed punishment for zinā, which does not apply here.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths from Ibn Abbas are cited: one commanding execution of both the man and the animal, the other stating there is no hadd.
Both are ahad hadiths, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The second hadith clearly negates hadd. The first hadith's command to kill is interpreted by Hanafis as a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) because hadd is exclusively for zinā. Thus the two are harmonized: no fixed hadd, but the judge may impose ta'zir up to execution.
This reconciliation avoids discarding either hadith.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may take the killing hadith literally as a hadd punishment or as mandatory execution. Hanafis maintain it is discretionary.
The disagreement arises from different methods of reconciling conflicting texts.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) because it upholds the principle that hadd is specific to zinā and avoids contradicting the explicit negation of hadd.
The animal is also killed to eliminate the source of sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَطِئَ قِيمَةً فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ. وَيُعَزِّرُ. وَجْهُ الدَّلِيلِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ أَتَى بَهِيمَةً فَاقْتُلُوهُ وَاقْتُلُوهَا مَعَهُ». وَعَن ابْن عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِي يَأْتِي الْبَهِيمَةَ حَدٌّ». (سنن ابوداود، نمبر 4465/4464; سنن ترمذي، نمبر 1455). أُصُول: بہیمہ اور جانور سے وطی کرنے والے کو حد نہیں البتہ بطور تعزیر کوئی بھی سزا دے حتی کہ تعزیر اقتل بھی کر اسکتا ہے۔
And whoever has intercourse with an animal, there is no hadd upon him, and he is punished with ta'zir. The face of the proof: From Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill it with him.' And from Ibn Abbas who said: 'There is no hadd upon the one who has intercourse with an animal.' (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). Usul: The one who has intercourse with an animal or beast receives no hadd; however, as ta'zir, any punishment may be given, even killing.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling covers bestiality. According to the Hanafi school, there is no fixed hadd penalty, but the offender is subject to ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The proof includes two apparently contradictory hadith from Ibn Abbas: one orders killing (both the man and the animal), and the other says there is no hadd. The Hanafis reconcile these by understanding the killing as ta'zir (discretionary, not fixed hadd). The judge may decide the severity; killing is permitted as a maximum ta'zir. The animal is also killed to remove the source of sin or prevent its use. The Urdu text clarifies that ta'zir can even include execution.

Key Terms
بَهِيمَةً (bahīmah): A beast or animal (any quadruped used for bestiality)
يُعَزِّرُ (yuʿazziru): He imposes ta'zir (discretionary punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on bestiality?
A) The offender is stoned to death as hadd.
B) The offender is given the same punishment as a fornicator.
C) No fixed hadd, but ta'zir (discretionary punishment) applies.
D) There is no legal consequence because it involves an animal.

Key Takeaway
Bestiality is not zinā; the Hanafi school holds that no fixed hadd applies, only discretionary ta'zir which may include execution.

Zina in Dar al-Harb: No Hadd Upon Return
Ruling on zinā committed in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for zina committed in Dar al-Harb and explain the territorial jurisdiction rationale.

Core Idea
Hadd penalties are territorial: acts outside Islamic jurisdiction are not punishable upon return.

This passage addresses a critical question of jurisdiction: if a Muslim commits zina while living in a non-Muslim or rebel territory, does he face hadd when he returns to Islamic lands? The Hanafi school holds that the penal authority of the Islamic state is territorial, not personal. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs from the early community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and territory
Note the act (zina) and the territories (Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Baghy) where it occurred.
2
State the ruling
The matn says: 'the hadd is not enforced upon him' upon return to Islamic lands.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the first proof (al-Hasan's statement)
Al-Hasan says four things are referred to the ruler (sultan): zakat, prayer, hudud, and judgment. This implies that hudud are a prerogative of the ruler within his territorial authority.
The authority of the ruler is territorial.
4
Analyze the second proof (Umar's letter)
Umar wrote that no commander should administer hadd until the army leaves the mountain pass, lest the offender join the enemy. This shows a pragmatic concern that hadd in enemy territory could drive a person to apostasy, and also implies that hadd is not meant to be applied there.
The rationale is both jurisdictional and practical.
5
Synthesize the rationale
Combine the proofs: hadd is a ruler's function within his domain; acts outside that domain are not subject to his penal authority. Therefore, no hadd upon return.
This is not about forgiveness but about jurisdiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ زَنَى فِي دَارِ الحَرْبِ أَوْ فِي دَارِ الْبَغْيِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَيْنَا لَمْ يُقَمْ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ. وَجْهُ الدَّلِيلِ: عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: أَرْبَعَةٌ إِلَى السُّلْطَانِ: الزَّكَاةُ وَالصَّلَاةُ وَالْحُدُودُ، وَالْقَضَاءُ. (مصنف ابن شيبه، نمبر 30328) وَكَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ أَلَّا يَجْلِدَنَّ أَمِيرُ جَيْشٍ وَلَا سَرِيَّةٍ أَحَدًا الْحَدَّ، حَتَّى يَطْلَعَ الدَّرْبَ (لِئَلَّا) تَحْمِلَهُ حَمِيَّةُ الشَّيْطَانِ أَنْ يَلْحَقَ بِالْكُفَّارِ. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، نمبر 30791)
And whoever commits zinā in the Abode of War (Dar al-Harb) or in the Abode of Rebellion (Dar al-Baghy) and then returns to us, the hadd is not enforced upon him. The face of the proof: From al-Hasan who said: Four things are referred to the ruler: Zakat, Prayer, Hudud, and Judgment. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) And Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote that no leader of an army or detachment should administer the hadd penalty to anyone until they come out of the pass, lest the passion of Satan lead him to join the disbelievers. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling is about territorial jurisdiction of hadd. According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim commits zinā while living in Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim territory where Islamic law is not enforced) or in Dar al-Baghy (rebel territory outside Islamic authority), and later returns to Islamic lands, the hadd penalty is not applied. Why? Because the act occurred in a land where Islamic penal law was not in force; therefore, jurisdiction for hadd does not retroactively apply. The proofs: al-Hasan's statement that enforcement of hadd belongs to the ruler (sultan) implies it is tied to his authority within his domain. Umar's instruction to army commanders shows a pragmatic concern: applying hadd in enemy territory might drive the offender to join the enemy. Thus, the Hanafi view is that hadd is suspended for sins committed outside the Islamic state's effective jurisdiction. This is based on the concept of dar al-harb as a sphere where Islamic punishments are not executed.

Key Terms
دَارِ الحَرْبِ (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not implemented
دَارِ الْبَغْيِ (dār al-baghy): Territory of rebels who reject the legitimate Imam but have their own authority

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hadd not enforced on a person who commits zinā in Dar al-Harb and then returns to Islamic lands?
A) Because the person has repented.
B) Because Islamic penal jurisdiction does not extend to acts committed outside its territory.
C) Because the hadd requires four witnesses from the time of the act.
D) Because Umar ibn al-Khattab forbade it absolutely.

Key Takeaway
Hadd penalties in Hanafi fiqh are territorial: acts committed outside the jurisdiction of an Islamic state are not subject to hadd upon re-entry.

No Hadd for Bestiality: Ta'zir Only
Ruling on bestiality with proof from hadith and ta'zir alternative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality, identify the supporting hadith, and explain the distinction between hadd and ta'zir.

Core Idea
Bestiality has no fixed hadd; the judge may impose ta'zir, even death.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a sensitive but legally defined crime. You will see how the school uses conflicting hadiths to derive a ruling: no fixed punishment, but discretionary severity. Understanding this distinction sharpens your grasp of hadd versus ta'zir principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Read the matn: 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, there is no hadd upon him.' The act is bestiality; the ruling is no hadd.
2
Locate the Dalil
The text cites two hadiths from Ibn Abbas. One commands killing both man and animal; the other explicitly negates hadd. Identify these as the evidence.
The second hadith is the primary proof for the Hanafi view.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The negation 'laysa alayhi hadd' is explicit. The command to kill is interpreted as ta'zir, not a fixed hadd, because it conflicts with the negation and hadd requires definitive proof.
Hanafi usul: a general command does not override an explicit negation when both are ahad.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Other schools (Maliki, Hanbali) take the killing command as a fixed hadd. Hanafis restrict hadd to the prescribed list.
The dispute hinges on how to reconcile conflicting ahadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: ta'zir, including possible execution, at the judge's discretion.
This balances the gravity of the sin with the principle that hadd requires clear textual basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَطِئَ بَهِيمَةً فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: مَنْ أَتَى بَهِيمَةً فَاقْتُلُوهُ وَاقْتُلُوهَا مَعَهُ
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِي يَأْتِي الْبَهِيمَةَ حَدٌّ
اصول: بہیمہ اور جانور سے وطی کرنے والے کو حد نہیں البتہ بطور تعزیر کوئی بھی سزا دے حتی کہ تعزیر اقتل بھی کر اسکتا ہے۔
And whoever has intercourse with an animal, there is no hadd upon him. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill it with him. From Ibn Abbas: There is no hadd upon the one who has intercourse with an animal. Principle: The one who has intercourse with an animal is not given hadd, but rather he is given ta'zir punishment, even up to execution as ta'zir.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Hudud presents the Hanafi ruling on bestiality. The matn states: 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, there is no hadd upon him.' This means the fixed prescribed punishment (hadd) does not apply, but the judge may administer a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) according to the severity of the crime, which could even be death. The proof is from a hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet said to kill both the man and the animal, but another narration from Ibn Abbas clarifies that no hadd is prescribed for this act. The Hanafi school reconciles these by taking the negation of hadd as the operative ruling, and the command to kill is understood as ta'zir, not a fixed hadd. The Urdu commentary further emphasizes that no hadd applies, but ta'zir may be severe.

Key Terms
بَهِيمَة (bahīmah): Any quadruped animal; specifically in this context, an animal used for bestiality.
تَعْزِير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or kaffarah.
حَدّ (ḥadd): Fixed Quranic or prophetic punishment for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He receives the hadd of zina (100 lashes).
B) No hadd applies, but he is subject to ta'zir.
C) He is executed immediately.
D) He is exiled for one year.

Key Takeaway
Bestiality is a major sin but not a hadd offense; the judge imposes ta'zir, potentially including death.

Zina in Dar al-Harb: No Hadd After Return
Ruling on zina committed in enemy territory and then returning to Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for zina committed in dar al-harb and explain the jurisdictional basis for waiving the hadd upon return.

Core Idea
Hadd is not applied for zina in dar al-harb because Islamic judicial authority was absent at the time of the act.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling regarding hudud jurisdiction. When a Muslim commits zina in enemy territory and later returns to dar al-Islam, the Hanafi school holds that no hadd is established. This ruling is based on the understanding that hudud are tied to the authority of the Islamic state, which was not present at the time of the crime. We will explore the textual evidence from the Companions and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the matn: whoever commits zina in dar al-harb or dar al-baghyi then returns, no hadd is established upon him.
The ruling is explicitly stated in the first line.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hadd should be applied upon return because the act is a sin punishable by hadd, regardless of location.
This is a legitimate difference of opinion.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof includes the statement of al-Hasan al-Basri that four matters are for the sultan (including hudud), and the practice of Umar and Abu al-Darda forbidding execution of hudud in enemy territory.
These indicate that hudud require the authority of the Islamic state.
4
Examine the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school relies on general texts commanding hadd for zina, without restricting to location.
Hanafis respond that these texts are general but are qualified by the jurisdictional principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi says no punishment; Shafi'i says hadd applies upon return.
This difference affects actual legal outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ زَنَى فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ أَوْ فِي دَارِ الْبَغْيِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَيْنَا لَمْ يُقَمْ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ
عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: أَرْبَعَةٌ إِلَى السُّلْطَانِ: الزَّكَاةُ وَالصَّلَاةُ وَالْحُدُودُ وَالْقَضَاءُ
كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ أَلَا يَجْلِدَنَّ أَمِيرُ جَيْشٍ وَلَا سَرِيَّةٍ أَحَدًا الْحَدَّ، حَتَّى يَطْلَعَ الدَّرْبَ (لِئَلَّا) تَحْمِلَهُ حَمِيَّةُ الشَّيْطَانِ أَنْ يَلْحَقَ بِالْكُفَّارِ
أَنَّ أَبَا الدَّرْدَاءِ نَهَى أَنْ يُقَامَ عَلَى أَحَدٍ حَدٌّ فِي أَرْضِ الْعَدُوِّ
And whoever commits zina in dar al-harb or dar al-baghyi then returns to us, hadd is not established upon him. From al-Hasan: Four matters are for the sultan: zakat, prayer, hudud, and judiciary. Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: 'No commander of an army or detachment should flog anyone with the hadd until he emerges from the pass, lest the zeal of Satan drive him to join the disbelievers.' Abu al-Darda forbade establishing any hadd on anyone in enemy territory.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage rules that if a Muslim commits zina in dar al-harb (enemy territory) or dar al-baghyi (territory of rebels) and then returns to dar al-Islam, the hadd is not applied. The reasoning is that Islamic judicial authority was not present at the time of the act. The proof includes a statement from al-Hasan al-Basri that hudud are under the sultan's authority, and the practice of Umar and Abu al-Darda who forbade executing hudud in enemy territory for fear of driving Muslims to apostasy. This is a Hanafi position; Imam al-Shafi'i is reported to disagree, holding that hadd should be applied after return. The text cites Umar's letter as proof for both sides, but the Hanafi interpretation prioritizes the absence of full legal authority.

Key Terms
دَار الْحَرْب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not fully implemented.
دَار الْبَغْي (dār al-baghyi): Territory controlled by rebels against the legitimate Islamic government.
الْحَدّ (al-ḥadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes.
السُّلْطَان (al-sulṭān): The ruler or governing authority with power to enforce Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim commits zina in dar al-harb and then returns to dar al-Islam, what happens?
A) He is given hadd immediately.
B) He is given ta'zir only.
C) No hadd is established upon him.
D) He is exiled.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is not established for crimes committed outside the jurisdiction of Islamic courts, even after returning to dar al-Islam.

The Hanafi Ruling on Liwat: Ta'zir vs. Hadd
Ruling on liwat with proof and disagreement among scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the punishment for liwat and explain why it differs from the position of other scholars.

Core Idea
Liwat is not zina; it is punished by ta'zir, not a fixed hadd.

This passage from Al-Quduri sets out the Hanafi view on punishing sodomy, contrasting it with the views of some early scholars. It presents a hadith that appears to command execution but interprets it as a discretionary punishment. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between fixed hudud and discretionary ta'zir.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the matn: 'yu'azziru' (he gives ta'zir). The Hanafi school treats liwat as a crime punishable by ta'zir, not a fixed hadd.
Ta'zir can be severe, including death, but it is discretionary.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The text mentions 'some scholars among the Tabi'in' and 'al-Thawri and the people of Kufa' who say the hadd of liwat is the hadd of zina (lashes for unmarried, death for married).
This is the opposing view within the same Kufan tradition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent relies on the hadith commanding killing and analogy with zina. They consider liwat a type of zina.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as a recommendation for severe ta'zir, not a fixed hadd, because the Quranic definition of zina is specific to vaginal intercourse with a woman. Hadd is restricted to that definition.
This is based on usul principles: the general command is overridden by the specific definition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, the judge decides the punishment (could be lashing, imprisonment, or execution). Under the opposing view, a fixed punishment is applied (lashes or death).
Practical difference in legal application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُعَزَّرُ مَنْ عَمِلَ عَمَلَ قَوْمِ لُوطٍ
رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ وَجَدْتُمُوهُ يَعْمَلُ عَمَلَ قَوْمٍ لُوطٍ، فَاقْتُلُوا الْفَاعِلَ، وَالْمَفْعُولُ بِهِ»
وَقَالَ بَعْضُ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ مِنْ فُقَهَاءِ التَّابِعِينَ: الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ، وَإِبْرَاهِيمُ النَّخَعِيُّ، وَعَطَاءُ بْنُ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ، وَغَيْرُهُمْ، قَالُوا: حَدُّ اللُّوطِيِّ حَدُّ الزَّانِي، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الثَّوْرِيِّ وَأَهْلِ الْكُوفَةِ
And he (the judge) gives ta'zir to the one who does the deed of the people of Lut. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whomever you find doing the deed of the people of Lut, kill the active and the passive partner.' And some scholars among the jurists of the Tabi'in, including al-Hasan al-Basri, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Ata ibn Abi Rabah, and others, said: The hadd of the sodomite is the hadd of the adulterer (zina). That is also the saying of al-Thawri and the people of Kufa.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on liwat (sodomy). The matn states: 'He gives ta'zir' meaning the judge has discretion. Then a hadith from the Prophet commands execution for both participants. However, the Hanafi school interprets this hadith as a severe form of ta'zir, not a fixed hadd. The passage then notes that some Tabi'in and Kufan scholars (like al-Thawri) hold that the hadd for liwat is the same as for zina (100 lashes for unmarried). The Hanafi position is that the punishment is ta'zir, which can be severe, but it is not the fixed hadd of zina. This is based on the principle that hadd is only for sexual intercourse that is specifically defined in the Quran (zina between a man and a woman).

Key Terms
لُوطِيّ (lūṭiyy): One who commits sodomy (the act of the people of Lut).
تَعْزِير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for sins not covered by hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Death by stoning.
C) Ta'zir, which may include severe punishment.
D) No punishment, only repentance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school punishes liwat with ta'zir, not hadd, because it does not fit the definition of zina.
