Hadd for Drinking: Conditions and Proofs
Rulings on hadd for drinking wine and nabidh with proofs from companions and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for applying hadd for drinking wine or nabidh and identify the proofs from the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking is established only if caught with smell or confesses while intoxicated; mere smell or vomiting does not trigger it.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking alcohol. The matn of al-Quduri specifies two alternative conditions for liability: being seized while the smell of wine is present with witnesses, or confessing while the smell is still there. The passage also clarifies that intoxication from nabidh (date/raisin drink) is treated the same as wine. Several hadith proofs from Umar, the Prophet's treatment of Nu'ayman, and a case of nabidh intoxication are cited. Understanding these conditions is crucial to correctly applying or withholding hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is drinking wine (khamr) or any intoxicant (nabidh). The ruling is that the perpetrator incurs hadd (80 lashes) according to the Hanafi school.
The text does not specify the number of lashes, but the Hanafi position is 80.
2
Identify the two alternative conditions for hadd
Condition A: The person is seized while the smell of wine is still present, and witnesses testify to the drinking. Condition B: The person confesses to drinking while the smell is still present. If neither condition is met, no hadd is applied.
Confession after the smell has dissipated is not sufficient.
3
Note the exceptions and edge cases
Mere smell of wine on a person without witnesses or confession does not trigger hadd. Vomiting wine also does not trigger hadd. Intoxication from nabidh is treated like wine for hadd purposes.
The text explicitly states 'There is no hadd on one from whom the smell of wine is found or who vomits it.'
4
Locate the proof (dalil)
The practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab flogging based on smell, the Prophet ordering the beating of Nu'ayman with palm branches for drunkenness, and the Prophet flogging a man drunk on nabidh. These establish that intoxication is punishable by flogging.
The hadith are from Sunan al-Daraqutni, Sahih al-Bukhari, and others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ حَدِّ الشُّرْبِ
وَمَنْ شَرِبَ الْخَمْرَ فَأُخِذَ وَرِيحُهَا مَوْجُودٌ فَشَهِدَ عَلَيْهِ الشُّهُودُ بِذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ. فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بَعْدَ ذَهَابِ رِيحِهَا لَمْ يُحَدَّ.
وَمَنْ سَكِرَ مِنَ النَّبِيدِ حُدَّ. وَلَا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وُجِدَ مِنْهُ رِيحُ الْخَمْرِ أَوْ تَقَيَّأَهَا.
عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ أَنَّهُ جَلَدَ رَجُلًا وَجَدَ مِنْهُ رِيحَ شَرَابٍ الْحَدَّ تَامًّا.
عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْنِ الْحَارِثِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِنُعَيْمَانَ وَهُوَ سَكْرَانُ فَأَمَرَ مَنْ فِي الْبَيْتِ أَنْ يَضْرِبُوهُ بِالْجَرِيدِ وَالنِّعَالِ.
عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ قَالَ: لَا يُؤَجَّلُ فِي الْحُدُودِ إِلَّا قَدْرَ مَا يُقَامُ الْقَاضِي.
عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِرَجُلٍ قَدْ سَكِرَ مِنْ نَبِيدِ قَرٍّ فَجَلَدَهُ.
اصول: شراب اور نشہ آور چیزوں کے پینے کو شرب کہتے ہیں، شریعت میں اس کے مرتکب پر حد ہوتی ہے۔ اصول: شرب خمر کی حد کی دو شرط ہیں اپنے کی حالت پکڑا گیا ہو اور منھ میں بد بو موجود ہو، یا اقرار کریں کہ خوشی سے پی ہے تب حد لگے گی۔
Chapter of Hadd for Drinking. Whoever drinks wine and is seized while its smell is present, and witnesses testify to that, then he has hadd upon him. But if he confesses after the smell has gone, he is not given hadd. Whoever becomes drunk from nabidh is given hadd. There is no hadd on one from whom the smell of wine is found or who vomits it. From Umar ibn al-Khattab that he flogged a man from whom he found the smell of drink, fully the hadd. From Uqbah ibn al-Harith that the Prophet was brought Nu'ayman while he was drunk, and he ordered those in the house to beat him with palm branches and sandals. From al-Sha'bi: 'No delay in hudud except to the extent of the qadi being set up.' From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah was brought a man who had become drunk on cold nabidh, and he flogged him. Principle: Drinking wine and intoxicants is called shurb; in Shariah, its perpetrator receives hadd. Principle: The hadd for drinking wine has two conditions: he is caught in a drunken state and the smell is present in his mouth, or he confesses that he drank willingly; then hadd is applied.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from Bab Hadd al-Shurb details the Hanafi rulings on punishment for drinking alcohol. The matn states that hadd (80 lashes) is applied if the person is caught with the smell of wine still present and witnesses testify. However, if the person confesses after the smell has dissipated, no hadd is given, because there is no corroborating physical evidence. Furthermore, anyone who gets drunk from nabidh (intoxicating drink from dates/raisins) is also given hadd. But if someone is merely found with the smell of wine or vomits it, hadd is not applied without other evidence. The hadith proofs include Umar's practice of flogging based on smell, the Prophet beating Nu'ayman with palm branches, and the Prophet flogging a man drunk on nabidh. The Urdu commentary summarizes that the conditions are being caught drunk or confessing after removing doubt.

Key Terms
نَبِيذ (nabīdh): An intoxicating drink made from dates, raisins, or other fruits.
شَرِبَ الخَمْرَ (shariba al-khamr): To drink wine (or any intoxicating beverage) – the act that triggers hadd.
الْحَدُّ (al-hadd): The fixed punishment prescribed by Shariah for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what are the conditions for establishing the hadd for drinking?
A) The person must be caught in the act of drinking.
B) The smell of wine must be present at seizure, or the person confesses while the smell is present.
C) The person must vomit wine.
D) The person must confess after the smell is gone.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking is only applied if the offender is caught with the smell of wine present or confesses while the smell is still there; otherwise, no hadd is imposed, as supported by the practice of the Prophet and Umar.

Hadd for Drinking Wine and Nabidh Intoxication
Stating the ruling on hadd for wine and nabidh, with conditions for proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that establish the hadd for drinking wine and nabidh, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Hadd requires immediate evidence of intoxication; delayed confession does not suffice.

In this passage from Al-Quduri's matn on hudud, we learn the precise conditions under which the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking wine or intoxicating nabidh is applied. The ruling emphasizes the importance of immediate evidence—the smell of drink or visible intoxication—and clarifies that a delayed confession does not trigger the penalty. Two hadith proofs from Umar and Ibn Umar support this position, showing that the Companions and the Prophet himself relied on sensory evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is drinking wine (khamr) or becoming intoxicated from nabidh. The ruling is that the hadd (80 lashes) is wajib upon the drinker.
The act itself is haram; the hadd is a separate penalty.
2
Locate the conditions for hadd
For wine: the drinker must be caught while the smell is present and witnesses testify. For nabidh: intoxication (sukr) must be established.
The smell is considered circumstantial proof.
3
Note the exception
If the person confesses after the smell has faded, the hadd is not applied. This prevents unreliable confessions.
This exception is specific to delayed confession.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Umar shows that finding the smell of drink is sufficient for flogging. The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet flogged a man for nabidh intoxication.
Both are ahad hadith with zanni thubut, but sufficient for establishing the ruling.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a confession without contemporaneous evidence is insufficient, unlike some other schools that may accept confession alone.
This protects against false confessions or exaggerated claims.

بَابُ حَدِّ الشُّرْبِ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: وَمَنْ شَرِبَ الْخَمْرَ فَأُخِذَ وَرِيحُهَا مَوْجُودٌ فَشَهِدَ عَلَيْهِ الشُّهُودُ بِذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ. فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بَعْدَ ذَهَابِ رِيحِهَا لَمْ يُحَدَّ. وَمَنْ سَكِرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ حُدَّ. وَلَا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وُجِدَ مِنْهُ رِيحُ الْخَمْرِ أَوْ تَقَيَّأَهَا. أصول: شراب اور نشہ آور چیزوں کے پینے کو شرب کہتے ہیں، شریعت میں اس کے مرتکب پر حد ہوتی ہے۔ أصول: شرب خمر کی حد کی دو شرط ہیں اپنے کی حالت پکڑا گیا ہو اور منھ میں بد بو موجود ہو، یا اقرار کریں کہ خوشی سے پی ہے تب حد لگے گی۔ عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ أَنَّهُ جَلَدَ رَجُلًا وَجَدَ مِنْهُ رِيحَ شَرَابٍ. (سنن دارقطني، كتاب الأشربة، رقم 4689). عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِرَجُلٍ قَدْ سَكِرَ مِنْ نَبِيذٍ فَجَلَدَهُ. (سنن دارقطني، كتاب الحدود، رقم 3357).
Chapter on the Hadd of Drinking. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Whoever drinks wine and is caught while its smell is still present, and witnesses testify to that, then the hadd is due upon him. If he confesses after the smell has faded, he is not subjected to hadd. And whoever becomes intoxicated from nabidh is subjected to hadd. And there is no hadd upon one from whom the smell of wine is found or who vomits it. Principle: Drinking wine and intoxicating substances is called shurb; in Shari'a, the perpetrator is liable to hadd. Principle: The hadd for wine-drinking has two conditions: that he be caught while intoxicated and the smell in his mouth is present, or he confesses that he drank willingly; then the hadd is applied. From Umar ibn al-Khattab that he flogged a man from whom he found the smell of drink. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Ashribah, no. 4689). From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought a man who had become intoxicated from nabidh and he flogged him. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hudud, no. 3357).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from Al-Quduri's matn on the chapter of hadd for drinking, followed by Urdu commentary and hadith proofs. The author states three rulings: (1) The hadd for wine is established only if the drinker is caught while the smell of wine is still detectable, and witnesses testify to that—the smell itself is considered circumstantial proof. (2) If the smell has faded and he confesses later, the hadd is not applied because the confession may be unreliable or he may have repented. (3) Becoming intoxicated from nabidh (a drink made from dates or grapes that is not inherently intoxicating but becomes so) also incurs the full hadd, because the prohibition is on intoxication, not the substance. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the hadd requires either being caught with the smell or a voluntary confession. The hadith of Umar shows that finding the smell of drink is sufficient for flogging, and the hadith of Ibn Umar shows that the Prophet himself flogged a man for intoxication from nabidh.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): The act of drinking intoxicating substances; in this context, it is the specific act that incurs the hadd punishment.
خمر (khamr): Wine made from grapes; its prohibition is explicit, and its hadd is established by clear texts.
نبيد (nabidh): A drink made from dates or other fruits that becomes intoxicating when left to ferment; its intoxication incurs the same hadd as wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the drinker is caught with the smell of wine on his breath
B) When the drinker confesses after the smell of wine has faded
C) When the drinker becomes intoxicated from nabidh
D) When witnesses testify to seeing him drink

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking is applied only when the drinker is caught with objective evidence of intoxication (smell or visible drunkenness), not on delayed confession alone.

Conditions for Hadd: Awareness, Volition, and Sobriety
Specifying conditions for applying hadd to a drunk person and the prescribed punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for applying the hadd for drinking, identify the prescribed punishment of eighty lashes, and explain the evidence from the practice of Umar (ra).

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking requires knowledge, volition, and sobriety; the punishment is eighty lashes.

This passage specifies the conditions under which the hadd (fixed punishment) for drinking is applied. It clarifies that the drunk person must have known the drink was intoxicating, must have drunk it voluntarily, and must be sober at the time of punishment. The punishment is eighty lashes, distributed over the body. The text also provides hadith evidence, including the practice of Umar (ra) in establishing the number of lashes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the first part: the drunk is not punished until (1) he knows he became intoxicated from the drink, (2) he drank it willingly (taw'an), and (3) his intoxication has passed. These are the preconditions for the hadd.
2
Recall the punishment amount and method
Note that the hadd for both wine and intoxicating nabidh is eighty lashes, and the beating is distributed over the body as in zina. This is the actual penalty.
3
Understand the principle from the Urdu commentary
The Urdu commentary adds: 'If intoxication occurs in a lawful substance, its drinking incurs hadd.' This means even a halal substance, if it becomes intoxicating, triggers the hadd.
4
Examine the first hadith evidence
The hadith of Ibn Umar shows that the Prophet delayed flogging until the man was sober, proving the condition of sobriety.
Reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi
5
Examine the second hadith evidence
The hadith of al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid indicates that during Umar's caliphate, the practice settled on eighty lashes, which became the standard for the Hanafi school.
Reference: Sahih al-Bukhari

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَانُ حَتَّى يَعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ سَكِرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ وَشَرِبَهُ طَوْعًا. وَلَا يُحَدُّ حَتَّى يَزُولَ عَنْهُ السُّكْرُ. وَحَدُّ الْخَمْرِ وَالسُّكْرِ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ فِي الْحَدِّ ثَمَانُونَ سَوْطًا يُفَرَّقُ الضَّرْبُ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ كَمَا ذُكِرَ فِي حَدِّ الزِّنَا. أصول: حلال چیز میں اگر نشہ پیدا ہو جائے تو اس کے شرب میں حد لگے گی۔ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِرَجُلٍ سَكْرَانَ فَلَمَّا ذَهَبَ سُكْرُهُ أَمَرَ بِجَلْدِهِ. (سنن بيهقي، باب ما جاء في إقامة الحد في حال السكر أو حتى يذهب سكره، رقم 17525). عَنِ السَّائِبِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ قَالَ: كُنَّا نُؤْتَى بِالشَّارِبِ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم... حَتَّى جَلَدَ عُمَرُ ثَمَانِينَ. (صحيح البخاري، باب الضرب بالجريد والنعال، رقم 6779).
And the drunk person is not subjected to hadd until he knows that he became intoxicated from nabidh and drank it willingly. And he is not subjected to hadd until his intoxication passes away. And the hadd for wine and intoxication from nabidh in the punishment is eighty lashes, the beating is distributed over his body as mentioned in the hadd of zina. Principle: If intoxication occurs in a lawful substance, then its drinking incurs hadd. From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought a drunk man, and when his intoxication passed, he ordered him to be flogged. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab... no. 17525). From al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: We used to bring the drinker at the time of the Messenger of Allah... until Umar flogged eighty. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-Darb bil-Jarid wal-Ni'al, no. 6779).
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson, adding three key conditions: (1) The drunk person must have knowledge that he became intoxicated from nabidh; this ensures that unintentional consumption is excluded. (2) He must have drunk it voluntarily (طوعا), excluding coercion. (3) The hadd is not applied until intoxication ends, because the person may not be aware of what is happening. The punishment is eighty lashes for both wine and intoxication from nabidh, administered in a way that distributes the lashes over the body to minimize harm, similar to the hadd for zina. The Urdu commentary explains that even lawful substances, if they become intoxicating, incur the hadd. The hadith of Ibn Umar shows that the Prophet delayed flogging until the man was sober. The hadith of al-Sa'ib shows that the number of lashes was standardized to eighty during Umar's caliphate based on consultation.

Key Terms
سكران (sakran): A person who is in a state of intoxication; the hadd is not applied while in this state, but after sobriety.
طوع (taw'an): Voluntarily, of one's own free will; coercion negates the hadd.
سوط (sawt): A whip; the unit of punishment in hadd. The plural is أسواط or سياط.

Key Takeaway

Conditions for Applying Hadd on a Drunkard
States conditions before hadd is applied and the prohibition of punishing while drunk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for applying the hadd punishment for drinking and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking is only applied after knowledge, willingness, and sobriety.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar sets the conditions that must be fulfilled before the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking intoxicants is carried out. The Hanafi school requires that the offender knew the drink was intoxicating, drank it willingly, and is sober at the time of punishment. The text provides evidence from the Quran, the practice of Umar, and the Prophet's Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the drunk is not punished (yuhadd) until certain conditions are met. The ruling is that hadd is wajib only when these conditions are satisfied.
2
List the conditions
Three conditions: 1) The person must know that the drink is intoxicating. 2) He must have drunk it willingly (not under duress). 3) The punishment is postponed until the intoxication wears off.
Knowledge and willingness exclude cases of ignorance or coercion.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Surah An-Nur 24:33 prohibits forcing slave girls into prostitution and states that if coercion occurs, Allah is Forgiving. The Hanafi school uses analogy: just as coercion removes blame, lack of knowledge also removes criminal intent.
The verse is cited as a basis for the principle that punishment requires intent.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The first hadith shows that Umar flogged a slave who forced a slave girl, but did not punish the girl because she was coerced. The second hadith shows that the Prophet ordered flogging of a drunk only after his intoxication passed.
Both hadiths reinforce the conditions of willingness and sobriety.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a judge must verify these conditions before ordering hadd. If any condition is missing, the hadd is not applied.
This protects against unjust punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَانُ حَتَّى يَعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ سَكِرَ مِنْ النَّبِيذِ وَشَرِبَهُ طَوْعًا وَلَا يُحَدُّ حَتَّى يَزُولَ عَنْهُ السُّكْرُ. وجه (1) الآية: ﴿وَلَا تُكْرِهُوا فَتَيَاتِكُمْ عَلَى الْبِغَاءِ إِنْ أَرَدْنَ تَحَصُّنًا لِتَبْتَغُوا عَرَضَ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَمَنْ يُكْرِهْهُنَّ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِكْرَاهِهِنَّ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ (سورة النور، 24:33). وجه (2) الحديث: أَنَّ صَفِيَّةَ ابْنَةَ أَبِي عُبَيْدٍ أَخْبَرَتْهُ أَنَّ عَبْدًا مِنْ رَقِيقِ الْإِمَارَةِ وَقَعَ عَلَى وَلِيدَةٍ مِنَ الْخُمُسِ فَاسْتَكْرَهَهَا حَتَّى اقْتَضَّهَا فَجَلَدَهُ عُمَرُ الْحَدَّ وَنَفَاهُ وَلَمْ يَجْلِدِ الْوَلِيدَةَ مِنْ أَجْلِ أَنَّهُ اسْتَكْرَهَهَا (رواه البخاري). وجه (3) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أُتِيَ بِرَجُلٍ سَكْرَانَ فَلَمَّا ذَهَبَ سُكْرُهُ أَمَرَ بِجَلْدِهِ (رواه البيهقي). اصول : حلال چیز میں اگر نشہ پیدا ہو جائے تو اس کے شرب میں حد لگے گی۔
And the drunk is not punished until he knows that he became intoxicated from nabidh and drank it willingly, and he is not punished until his intoxication passes. Proof (1) the verse: 'And do not compel your slave girls to prostitution...' (Surah An-Nur 24:33). Proof (2) the hadith: Safiyyah bint Abi Ubaid informed him that a slave of the government had intercourse with a slave girl from the khums and forced her, so Umar flogged him the hadd and exiled him, and did not flog the slave girl because he forced her (narrated by Bukhari). Proof (3) the hadith: From Ibn Umar that the Prophet was brought a drunk man, and when his intoxication left, he ordered his flogging (narrated by Bayhaqi). Principle: A hadd is imposed for drinking a permissible substance when it becomes intoxicating.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage states the conditions for applying the hadd punishment for drinking. The hadd is not applied to a drunk person until he knows that the drink he consumed is intoxicating (i.e., from nabidh) and that he drank it willingly. This excludes cases of duress or mistake. Additionally, the punishment is delayed until the person sobers up, as he cannot understand the proceedings while intoxicated. The Quranic verse cited (24:33) establishes that coercion removes guilt, and the hadith about Umar shows that the coerced slave girl was not punished. The hadith of Ibn Umar confirms that punishment is only after sobriety. The Urdu note adds that a permissible drink can also incur hadd if it becomes intoxicating.

Key Terms
السَّكْرَانُ (al-sakran): A person who is intoxicated, having consumed an intoxicant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) After he sobers up and knew he drank willingly
C) Only if he confesses
D) Only if four witnesses testify

Key Takeaway
Hadd for drinking requires knowledge, willingness, and sobriety before punishment.

The Hadd for Drinking Wine: 80 Lashes for a Free Person
Ruling with two proofs (hadith and companion statement)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd punishment for a free person who drinks wine or intoxicating nabidh, and describe the method of flogging as established by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The hadd for a free person's intoxication is 80 lashes, distributed over the body, a punishment settled by Umar's ijtihad and adopted by consensus.

This lesson examines the fixed punishment (hadd) for a free person who consumes wine or any intoxicating drink (nabidh). The text specifies 80 lashes and describes how the flogging should be administered: spread over the body, avoiding the face and private parts. We will also look at the two proofs: the practice of Umar (ra) and the instruction of Ali (ra).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states the hadd for a free person who drinks wine or intoxicating nabidh is 80 lashes. Note that the punishment differs for slaves (40 lashes, not mentioned here but known from other texts).
The ruling applies only to free persons; slaves receive half.
2
Understand the method of flogging
The flogging must be distributed over the body ('يُفَرَّقُ الضَّرْبُ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ') similar to the method for the hadd of zina, avoiding the face and genitals as per Ali's instruction.
This ensures the punishment is effective but not excessively harmful.
3
Analyze the first proof (hadith)
The hadith of as-Sa'ib ibn Yazid shows the evolution: originally informal strikes, then Umar set 40 lashes, then increased to 80 when people became brazen. This shows the sunnah settled at 80 by ijtihad with consensus.
The increase was a companion consensus (ijma') tacitly approved.
4
Analyze the second proof (saying of Ali)
Ali's instruction provides the practical method: give each limb its due, avoid the face and genitals. This is a companion statement (qawl sahabi) and is accepted as proof in Hanafi usul.
Qawl sahabi is a valid source when not contradicted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحَدُّ الخَمْرِ وَالسُّكْرِ مِنْ النَّبِيذِ فِي الْحُرِّ ثَمَانُونَ سَوْطًا يُفَرَّقُ الضَّرْبُ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ كَمَا ذُكِرَ فِي حَدِ الزِّنَا. وجه (1) الحديث: عَنِ السَّائِبِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ قَالَ: كُنَّا نُؤْتَى بِالشَّارِبِ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَإِمْرَةِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ وَصَدْرًا مِنْ خِلَافَةِ عُمَرَ فَتَقُومُ إِلَيْهِ بِأَيْدِينَا وَنِعَالِنَا وَأَرْدِيَتِنَا حَتَّى كَانَ آخِرُ إِمْرَةِ عُمَرَ فَجَلَدَ أَرْبَعِينَ حَتَّى إِذَا عَتَوْا وَفَسَقُوا جَلَدَ ثَمَانِينَ (رواه البخاري ومسلم). وجه (2) قول الصحابي: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: أُتِيَ بِرَجُلٍ سَكْرَانَ فَقَالَ: «اضْرِبْ وَأَعْطِ كُلَّ عُضْوٍ حَقَّهُ وَاتَّقِ الْوَجْهَ وَالْمَذَاكِيرَ» (رواه ابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق).
The hadd of wine and intoxication from nabidh for a free person is eighty lashes; the flogging is distributed over his body as mentioned in the hadd of zina. Proof (1) the hadith: From as-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: We used to bring the drinker at the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and early part of Umar's caliphate, and we would strike him with our hands, sandals, and garments, until the end of Umar's caliphate, he flogged forty. When they became insolent and immoral, he flogged eighty (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). Proof (2) the saying of the companion: Ali said: A drunk man was brought, so he said: 'Strike and give every limb its due, and avoid the face and genitals.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage establishes the hadd for a free person who drinks wine or intoxicating nabidh: 80 lashes. The flogging should be distributed over the body, not concentrated on one spot, similar to the method for the hadd of zina. The hadith shows that the original practice was less formal (40 lashes with various objects), but Umar later standardized it to 80 lashes by ijtihad when people became brazen. The second proof from Ali provides the method: avoid the face and private parts, and ensure each body part receives its share.

Key Terms
الحَرِّ (al-hurr): The free person as opposed to a slave.
الخَمْرِ (al-khamr): Wine or any intoxicating drink made from grapes.
السُّكْرِ (al-sukr): Intoxication; the state of being drunk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hadd for a free person for drinking wine according to the Hanafi school?
A) 40 lashes
B) 80 lashes
C) 100 lashes
D) Stoning

Key Takeaway
The hadd for a free person's drinking is 80 lashes, administered with distribution over the body and avoidance of face and genitals.

Hadd for a Slave Drinking Wine: 40 Lashes
Specifies half the free penalty for a slave: 40 lashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd punishment for a slave drinking wine (40 lashes), cite the two proofs (Quran verse 4:25 and practice of the Caliphs), and explain the Hanafi application of the half-rule to all hudud.

Core Idea
A slave receives 40 lashes for drinking wine—half the free person's punishment.

This passage addresses the fixed punishment (hadd) for a slave who drinks wine. The text clearly states the amount: 40 lashes. It then provides two proofs: the Quranic verse about half punishment for slave women in adultery, and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs who applied half the free hadd to their slaves. This lesson examines these proofs and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a slave drinking wine; the ruling is 40 lashes (half of the free person's 80).
2
Locate the first proof (Quran)
Surah An-Nisa 4:25: 'If they commit indecency, then upon them half the punishment of the free women.'
The verse speaks of slave women and zina, but serves as a general principle.
3
Explain wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi school uses qiyas jaliy (clear analogy): the half-rule applies to all hudud for slaves, including drinking, because the illa (effective cause) is slavery and the verse sets a principle of half punishment.
The verse's wording is general; 'fahishah' can encompass major sins.
4
Locate the second proof (companion practice)
The practice of Caliphs Umar, Uthman, and Abdullah ibn Umar is cited: they flogged their slaves 40 lashes for drinking.
This is considered strong evidence (qawl sahabi) in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) limit the half-rule to zina only; the Hanafi school extends it to all hudud. The mufta bihi is 40 lashes.

The practice of the Caliphs Umar, Uthman, and Abdullah ibn Umar confirms that slaves receive 40 lashes instead of 80. The Hanafi school consistently applies this half-rule to all hudud punishments for slaves.

Retraction of Confession Drops Hadd Punishment
States that if a person confesses then retracts, the hadd is not applied.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction after confession, identify the proof from hadith, and explain the rationale of doubt (shubha) averting punishment.

Core Idea
Retraction after confession creates legal doubt (shubha) that overrides the hadd punishment.

Confession is a strong proof in hudud cases, but the Hanafi school grants the accused a significant right: to retract the confession at any time before the punishment is carried out. Even if the confession was made voluntarily before the judge, a retraction creates a sufficient legal doubt (shubha) that the hadd is not applied. This ruling is rooted in the prophetic practice encouraging repentance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is confessing to a hadd offense (e.g., drinking wine) and then retracting. The ruling is that the hadd is not applied.
The ruling applies even if the confession was made in court.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith from the case of Ma'iz: 'Why did you not leave him, perhaps he may repent and Allah will forgive him?' This indicates that retraction should be accepted.
This is a sunnah ahad report, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Understand the rationale
Retraction introduces doubt (shubha) about the guilt. In Hanafi fiqh, hudud punishments are averted by doubts.
The doubt does not have to be strong; even a mere retraction suffices.
4
Note the scope and conditions
The ruling applies to all hudud, not just drinking. Retraction is accepted anytime before the actual execution of the punishment.
If retraction occurs after the punishment, it is irrelevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ وَالسُّكْرِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُحَدَّ. وجه (1) الحديث: هَلَّا تَرَكْتُمُوهُ لَعَلَّهُ أَنْ يَتُوبَ فَيَتُوبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ (رواه البيهقي والترمذي).
And whoever confesses to drinking wine and intoxication, then retracts, is not punished. Proof (1) the hadith: 'Why did you not leave him, perhaps he may repent and Allah will forgive him?' (narrated by Bayhaqi and Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of retraction after confession. If a person confesses to drinking (and by extension other hudud), then retracts, the hadd is not applied. The proof is the hadith regarding the case of Ma'iz (for zina) where the Prophet indicated that retraction should be accepted. The Hanafi school applies this principle to drinking and other hudud: retraction is accepted as a doubt that averts the punishment. The ruler should encourage the person to repent.

Key Terms
أَقَرَّ (aqarra): Confessed voluntarily before the court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Proof of Hadd: Two Witnesses or One Confession
Statement of proof for hadd of drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of proving hadd for drinking and explain why women's testimony is not accepted in hudud.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking is proven by two male witnesses or one confession; women's testimony is excluded by sunnah.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes the evidentiary requirements for the hadd punishment for drinking alcohol. While the Quranic verse about testimony is general, the sunnah specifies that hudud require male witnesses. The passage also clarifies that a single confession suffices, unlike in some other crimes. Understanding these rules ensures the hadd is applied correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is drinking alcohol (shurb) which carries a hadd punishment. The ruling is that this hadd is established under specific evidentiary conditions.
2
Identify the two methods of proof
The text states the hadd is proven by two witnesses (shahidayn) or by one confession (iqrar). Note that confession is accepted only once, not four times as in zina.
The Urdu note adds that if a witness retracts, the hadd is dropped.
3
Analyze the dalil from Quran and Sunnah
The Quranic verse (2:282) commands two male witnesses or one man and two women for general testimony. The sunnah, as reported by az-Zuhri, excludes women's testimony in hudud. This limits the verse's application.
The hadith from Ali (RA) shows the practice of cutting the hand of a thief based on two witnesses.
4
Understand the exclusion of women's testimony
The sunnah explicitly states that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud. Therefore, the witnesses must be male for hadd cases.
5
Distinguish from other hudud
Unlike zina which requires four witnesses, drinking requires only two. Also, for theft, two witnesses are needed, but with conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ أَوْ بِإِقْرَارِهِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً. وجه (1) الآية: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِنْ رِجَالِكُمْ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُونَا رَجُلَيْنِ فَرَجُلٌ وَامْرَأَتَانِ...﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2:282). وجه (2) قول التابعي: جَاءَ رَجُلَانِ بِرَجُلٍ إِلَى عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ فَشَهِدَا عَلَيْهِ بِالسَّرِقَةِ فَقَطَعَهُ (رواه الدارقطني). وجه (3) قول التابعي: عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ: مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الْحُدُودِ (رواه ابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق). اصول : حد شرب کے لئے دو گواہ چاہئے زنا کی طرح چار گواہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ، نیز گواہ رجوع کرے توحد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
And it is established by the testimony of two witnesses or by his confession once. Proof (1) the verse: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men, if not two men then one man and two women...' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:282). Proof (2) the saying of the Tabi'iyy: Two men brought a man to Ali ibn Abi Talib and testified against him for theft, so he cut off his hand (narrated by Daruqutni). Proof (3) the saying of the Tabi'iyy: From az-Zuhri: The sunnah from the Prophet and the two caliphs after him has passed that the testimony of women is not accepted in hudud (narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abdurrazzaq). Principle: For the hadd of drinking, two witnesses are required; unlike zina where four are needed. Also, if a witness retracts, the hadd is dropped.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains how the hadd for drinking is proven: by two male witnesses or by the offender's confession once. Unlike zina which requires four witnesses, drinking requires only two. The Quranic verse cited is about general testimony, but the specific requirement for hudud is clarified by sunnah and practice. The ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud is a well-known principle. The Urdu note adds that if a witness retracts, the hadd drops. This is consistent with the previous lesson on retraction.

Key Terms
إِقْرَارِهِ (iqrarihi): The confession of the offender himself.
شَاهِدَيْنِ (shahidayn): Two witnesses (dual form).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Hadd of a Slave for Drinking Wine is 40 Lashes
Ruling on the hadd of a slave for drinking wine, with scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hadd punishment for a slave found guilty of drinking wine (40 lashes) and identify the two scriptural proofs (Quran 4:25 and Companion practice) that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
A slave's hadd for drinking is 40 lashes — half the free person's, derived from Quranic analogy and Caliphal practice.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Al-Quduri's matn: the fixed punishment (hadd) for a slave who drinks wine. The text states the quantity (40 lashes) and then provides two proofs: a verse from Surah al-Nisa and the practice of the early Caliphs. Understanding this ruling helps you see how Hanafi fiqh uses textual proof (naql) and analogy (qiyas) to derive hudud punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. The act is a slave drinking wine; the ruling is that the hadd is 40 lashes (a wajib punishment fixed by revelation).
The hadd is a fixed punishment; its quantity cannot be changed by judicial discretion.
2
Locate the first dalil (Quranic verse)
The text cites Quran 4:25, which prescribes half the punishment of a free woman for a slave woman guilty of zinā. Note that this verse directly addresses zinā, not drinking. The Hanafi school applies it by analogy (qiyas) to the case of drinking.
The verse is qati' al-thubut (definitely transmitted) but zanni al-dalala (the analogy is interpretive).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (the legal link)
The underlying cause (ʿilla) is slave status, which reduces legal capacity and thus halves the punishment. Since the ʿilla is common to both zinā and drinking, the half-punishment principle extends to the hadd for drinking.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the ʿilla is evident.
4
Locate the second dalil (Companion practice)
The text reports that Umar ibn al-Khattab, Uthman ibn Affan, and Abdullah ibn Umar flogged their slaves 40 lashes for drinking. This establishes a binding precedent (sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs).
The Hanafi school considers the practice of the Caliphs as a source of law when it is unanimous and not contradicted by other evidence.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Based on the Quranic principle and the Companion practice, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that a slave's hadd for drinking is 40 lashes. This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Other schools may differ on the exact number but the half‑punishment principle is widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ حَدِ الشَّرْبِ
وَإِنْ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَحَدُّهُ أَرْبَعُونَ سَوْطًا
وَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَحَدُّهُ أَرْبَعُونَ سَوْطًا ﴿فَإِنْ أَتَيْنَ بِفَاحِشَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِنَّ نِصْفُ مَا عَلَى الْمُحْصَنَاتِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ﴾ سورة النساء، آية 25
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَحَدُّهُ أَرْبَعُونَ سَوْطًا عَنِ ابْنِ شِهَابٍ، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ جَلْدِ الْعَبْدِ فِي الْخَمْرِ فَقَالَ: بَلَغَنَا أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ نِصْفَ جَلْدِ الْحُرِّ، وَأَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ وَعُثْمَانَ بْنَ عَفَّانَ وَعَبْدَ اللهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ قَدْ جَلَدُوا عَبِيدَهُمْ نِصْفَ حَدِّ الْحُرِّ فِي الْخَمْرِ، (سنن البيهقي، باب ما جاء في عدد حد الخمر، رقم 17548)
Chapter of the hadd of drinking. And if he is a slave, then his hadd is forty lashes. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that if a slave, his hadd is forty lashes: 'And if they commit lewdness, then upon them half the punishment of the free women' (Surah al-Nisa, 4:25). Evidence (2): The saying of the Companion for establishing that if a slave, his hadd is forty lashes: From Ibn Shihab that he was asked about flogging a slave for drinking and he said: It has reached us that upon him is half the flogging of a free person, and that Umar ibn al-Khattab, Uthman ibn Affan, and Abdullah ibn Umar flogged their slaves half the hadd of a free person for drinking (Sunan al-Bayhaqi).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri, followed by its proofs. The ruling: a slave's hadd for drinking wine is 40 lashes, half of a free person's 80. The first proof is a Quranic verse regarding slave women, applied by analogy (qiyas) to male slaves: just as the hadd for unlawful sexual intercourse for a slave woman is half that of a free woman, the same reduction applies to the hadd for drinking. The second proof is the practice of the righteous caliphs Umar and Uthman, and the Companion Ibn Umar, who enacted this half-hadd on their slaves. This establishes the Hanafi position firmly within the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Key Terms
حَدّ (ḥadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by the Qur'an and Sunnah for specific crimes (drinking, theft, zinā, etc.).
عَبْد (ʿabd): A male slave; in Islamic law, a human being owned by another, with limited legal capacity and reduced punishments compared to a free person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the hadd for a slave drinking wine at 40 lashes, half of the free person's punishment, based on Quranic analogy and the established practice of the righteous Caliphs.

Retraction of Confession Nullifies Hadd for Drinking
Ruling on the effect of retracting a confession for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession for drinking and apply the principle that retraction drops the hadd to encourage repentance.

Core Idea
A confession to a hadd can be retracted, and the punishment is dropped to encourage repentance.

In Hanafi fiqh, the door of repentance is kept wide open. This lesson examines a specific ruling where a person who confesses to drinking wine then retracts that confession is not punished. This reflects the Prophetic instruction to leave the confessor in hope of divine forgiveness. We will explore the evidence and the legal reasoning behind this leniency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a confession (iqrār) to drinking wine or being intoxicated, followed by a retraction (rujūʿ). The ruling: the hadd punishment (80 lashes) is not applied.
The confession must be voluntary and before a judge.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from the incident of Māʿiz (who confessed to zinā). The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Did you not leave him? Perhaps he may repent, and Allah will accept his repentance.' This is extended by qiyās to drinking.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's instruction implies that retraction should be accepted to encourage repentance. Since the hadd is to purify the sinner, if retraction indicates possible repentance, the punishment is dropped.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle of 'doubt repels the hadd'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shāfiʿī) require two confessions for hudud and also accept retraction but may have stricter conditions. The Hanafi view is more flexible.
The disagreement is about the number of confessions required for a valid hadd.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the general principle of dropping hadd in cases of doubt and the explicit command to leave Māʿiz. This position is muftā bihī.
The authority weight is Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ، وَالسُّكْرِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُحَدَّ
وَجْهٌ: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ إِلَّا تَرَكْتُمُوهُ لَعَلَّهُ أَنْ يَتُوبَ، فَيَتُوبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ، (سنن البيهقي، باب رجم ماعز بن مالك، رقم 4419 / سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في درء الحد عن المعترف إذا رجع، رقم 1428)
And whoever confesses to drinking wine and intoxication, then retracts, he is not flogged. Evidence: The hadith for establishing that: 'Did you not leave him, perhaps he may repent, and Allah will accept his repentance.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Sunan al-Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a person confesses to drinking wine (or being drunk) and later retracts that confession, the hadd punishment is not applied. This is based on the principle of in dubio pro reo (benefit of the doubt) and the desire for repentance. The proof cited is a hadith from the incident of Māʿiz (the man who confessed to zinā), where the Prophet ﷺ encouraged leaving him to repent. By analogy, the same applies to drinking. The Hanafi school strongly upholds this 'drop the hadd in cases of doubt' principle.

Key Terms
إِقْرَار (iqrār): A voluntary confession or admission before a judge establishing liability for a hadd or other legal claim.
رُجُوع (rujūʿ): Withdrawal or retraction of a confession; in hadd cases, it nullifies the confession and prevents the punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He is flogged 40 lashes as a concession
C) The hadd is dropped and he is not flogged
D) He must pay a fine instead

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a retraction of a confession for a hadd crime nullifies the punishment, reflecting the priority of repentance and doubt over rigid application of penalties.

Proof of Hadd for Drinking: Witnesses and Confession
Ruling on proof of hadd for drinking: two male witnesses or a single confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for proving the hadd for drinking and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of confessions required.

Core Idea
For the hadd of drinking, two male witnesses or one confession suffices; Abu Yusuf required two confessions.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes a key procedural rule for the hadd punishment for drinking (shurb al-khamr). Unlike zina which requires four witnesses, the Hanafi school demands only two male witnesses, or a single confession from the accused. However, an important internal disagreement emerged between Abu Hanifa and his disciple Abu Yusuf on the sufficiency of one confession. We will examine the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the matn: the hadd for drinking is established by two male witnesses or a single confession.
No mention of a specific number of witnesses beyond two; confession is explicitly 'once'.
2
Identify the opposing view
Note that Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) held that two confessions are necessary, based on the practice of Caliph Ali.
This is an intra-madhhab difference, not an inter-madhhab one.
3
Examine the proofs
Review the Quranic verse (2:282) requiring two witnesses, the hadith of the thief who confessed once, and the practice of Ali. Understand how each proof supports the respective positions.
The Quranic verse is general; the Hanafis apply it by analogy to all hudud except zina.
4
Apply the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi (relied upon) view: the matn and the majority of Hanafi scholars prefer Abu Hanifa's position that one confession is sufficient.
The inclusion of Abu Yusuf's evidence indicates awareness of the difference, but the text itself gives the ruling as one confession.
5
Assess the practical consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: if someone confesses once, according to the mufta bihi, the hadd is wajib; according to Abu Yusuf, it is not until a second confession.
This affects judicial proceedings and the rights of the accused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ أَوْ بِإِقْرَارِهِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً
وَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِن رِجَالِكُمْ﴾ سورة البقرة، آية 282
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ جَاءَ رَجُلَانِ بِرَجُلٍ إِلَى عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ فَشَهِدَا عَلَيْهِ بِالسَّرِقَةِ فَقَطَعَهُ (الدارقطني)
وَجْهٌ: (٣) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الْحُدُودِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، مصنف عبد الرزاق)
وَجْهٌ: (٤) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ أُتِيَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ بِسَارِقٍ فَقَالَ لَا إِخَالُهُ سَرَقَ فَقَالَ بَلَى يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ قَدْ سَرَقْتُ قَالَ اذْهَبُوا بِهِ فَاقْطَعُوهُ (سنن البيهقي، سنن النسائي)
وَجْهٌ: (١) دَلِيلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ رَأَيْتُ عَلِيًّا أَقَرَّ عِنْدَهُ سَارِقٌ مَرَّتَيْنِ فَقَطَعَ يَدَهُ (سنن البيهقي)
وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ أَنَّ يَعْلَى بْنَ أُمَيَّةَ قَالَ قُلْتُ لِعُمَرَ إِنَّا بِأَرْضٍ فِيهَا شَرَابٌ كَثِيرٌ فَكَيْفَ تَجْلِدُهُ قَالَ إِذَا اسْتَقْرَىٰ أُمَّ الْقُرْآنِ فَلَمْ يَقْرَأْهَا وَلَمْ يَعْرِفْ رِدَاءَهُ فَاحْدُدْهُ (مصنف عبد الرزاق)
And it is established by the testimony of two witnesses or by his confession once. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing 'by the testimony of two witnesses': 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:282). Evidence (2): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'by the testimony of two witnesses': Two men brought a man to Ali ibn Abi Talib and testified against him for theft, and he cut off his hand (al-Daraqutni). Evidence (3): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'by the testimony of two witnesses': From al-Zuhri, he said: The Sunnah from the Messenger of Allah and the two Caliphs after him continued that women's testimony is not permitted in hudud (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). Evidence (4): The hadith for establishing 'by the testimony of two witnesses': From Abu Hurairah, he said: A thief was brought to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'I do not think he stole.' The man said: 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah, I stole.' He said: 'Take him and cut off his hand' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Sunan al-Nasa'i). Evidence (1) of Abu Yusuf: The saying of the Companion: I saw Ali when a thief confessed before him twice, and he cut off his hand and hung it around his neck (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Evidence (2): The saying of the Tabi'i for establishing 'by the testimony of two witnesses': That Yala ibn Umayyah said: I said to Umar: 'We are in a land where there is much drink (i.e., Yemen). How do you flog him?' He said: 'If he recites Umm al-Qur'an and does not recite it, and does not recognize his garment, then flog him' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence and also involves an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of confessions required. The matn from Al-Quduri states that the hadd for drinking is proven by the testimony of two male witnesses (not four, as required for zinā) or by a single confession from the accused. The commentary brings several proofs: a Quranic ayah about two witnesses (though it is from the verse on debt, applied by analogy to hudud), the practice of Ali who accepted two witnesses for theft, the statement of Zuhri that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, and a hadith about a thief confessing once and being punished. Notably, the text also includes a proof attributed to Abu Yusuf (Abu Hanifa's disciple) showing that Ali accepted a confession only after two occurrences, implying that Abu Yusuf required two confessions for hadd. The second proof from Umar discusses establishing intoxication. The overall Hanafi position is that one confession suffices, but Abu Yusuf's view (two confessions) is noted. The practical result: according to the mufta bihi (preferred view) of the Hanafi school, a single confession triggers the hadd, but the judge should encourage retraction to allow repentance.

Key Terms
شَهَادَة (shahāda): Testimony given in court; for hudud, it must be from two male witnesses who are just.
إِقْرَار (iqrār): Confession; for hadd of drinking, one confession is sufficient in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many witnesses are required to prove the hadd for drinking in the Hanafi school?
A) Four male witnesses
B) Two male witnesses
C) One male witness and two women
D) Two male witnesses or one confession

Key Takeaway
A single confession or two male witnesses establish the hadd for drinking; the judge must apply the punishment, though the accused may retract before execution.

Women's Testimony in Hudud: Inadmissibility and Its Proof
Ruling that women's testimony is inadmissible in hudud cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony in hudud and identify the proof from the Sunnah and the rationale behind the rule.

Core Idea
In hudud, women's testimony is completely inadmissible because such offenses are rights of Allah and women's testimony is considered deficient.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes a key procedural rule in Islamic criminal law: women's testimony cannot be used to prove hudud offenses, even when accompanied by male witnesses. The proof is a report from al-Zuhri that the Prophet and the two caliphs after him consistently rejected such testimony. The reasoning is that hudud are rights of Allah requiring the highest standard of proof, and women's testimony is considered to have a deficiency (naqṣ) in such matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on women's testimony in hudud? The text states it is not accepted (lā yuqbal).
This is a clear prohibition of admissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of al-Zuhri that the established Sunnah of the Prophet and the two caliphs was to reject women's testimony in hudud.
The report is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ' indicates a continuous, binding practice. This precedent from the Prophet and the caliphs establishes the rule.
The report is considered a proof from the Sunnah (though not mutawatir).
4
Understand the rationale
The text gives the reason: hudud are rights of Allah, and women's testimony has a deficiency (naqṣ) in such matters.
This rationale explains the strict rule and distinguishes hudud from other cases.
5
Note cross-madhhab agreement
Most schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) also reject women's testimony in hudud, though some later Hanafis allowed it in exceptional circumstances.
The relied-upon view (muftā bihī) is prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْقَبَلُ فِيهِ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ
لَا وَجْهَ: (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الْحُدُودِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، مصنف عبد الرزاق)
أُصُولٌ: الْحُدُودُ فِيَّ لَا يُقْبَلُ فِيهَا شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ، وَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ الْمُرْتَكَبَ حَقٌّ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَشَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِيهَا نَقْصٌ.
And the testimony of women with men is not accepted in it. No face: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i from al-Zuhri who said: The Sunnah from the Messenger of Allah and the two caliphs after him continued that the testimony of women is not permitted in hudud (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). Principles: In hudud, the testimony of women with men is not accepted, because the offense is a right of Allah, and the testimony of women in it has a deficiency.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, specifically a principle: women's testimony is inadmissible in hudud cases. The proof is the statement of al-Zuhri that the established Sunnah of the Prophet and the caliphs Umar and Uthman was to reject women's testimony in hudud. The Urdu note (صول) explains the reason: hudud are rights of Allah, and women's testimony is considered deficient in such matters, likely due to the lesser evidentiary requirements for hudud compared to financial transactions where women's testimony is accepted alongside men's.

Key Terms
شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ (shahādat al-nisāʾ): The testimony of women; in hudud, it is not accepted at all, even with male witnesses.
حَقُّ اللَّهِ (ḥaqq Allāh): A right belonging to Allah, i.e., a public order offense; hudud are considered divine rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the Quran forbids women testifying in any case

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony in hudud is completely inadmissible because hudud are rights of Allah requiring the highest standard of proof.

Establishment of Hadd for Drinking by Two Witnesses
Provides proofs for the ruling that hadd al-shurb is proven by two male witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the proof required for the hadd of drinking and explain the evidence from the Sunnah, the practice of the Companions, and the Tabi'un.

Core Idea
Hadd punishments require rigorous proof: two male witnesses or confession; the Hanafi school adheres strictly to this standard.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the fixed punishment (hadd) for consuming alcohol is established by the testimony of two male witnesses. The passage from Sharh al-Quduri presents multiple proofs: a prophetic hadith about a thief, the practice of Caliph Ali, and a statement of Umar. These collectively demonstrate the principle that hudud are proven by clear, unambiguous testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: the hadd for drinking is established by the testimony of two male witnesses.
2
Examine the first proof (Hadith)
Read the hadith from Abu Huraira about a thief. Though it involves theft, it demonstrates that a hadd punishment follows a clear admission or testimony.
Notice the Prophet's caution: 'I do not think he stole' — he required a clear admission.
3
Examine the second proof (Companion action)
Consider the action of Ali: he cut off a thief's hand after two confessions. This supports the principle that hudud need clear evidence.
The confession is like testimony.
4
Examine the third proof (Tabi'i statement)
Study Umar's instruction to Ya'la: the hadd for drinking is applied when the drinker fails to recite the Fatihah correctly or recognize his garment, indicating the need for evidence of intoxication.
This implies that testimony about his state is required.
5
Synthesize the proofs
Recognize that all three proofs converge on the requirement of clear evidence — two witnesses or confession — for establishing a hadd.
The Hanafi school does not accept women's testimony in hudud.

Source Text

وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ 
 عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: أُتِيَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِسَارِقٍ سَرَقَ شَمْلَةً، فَقَالُوا: إِنَّ هَذَا سَرَقَ، فَقَالَ: " لَا إِخَالُهُ سَرَقَ " فَقَالَ: بَلَى يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ قَدْ سَرَقْتُ، قَالَ : " اذْهَبُوا بِهِ فَاقْطَعُوهُ، ثُمَّ احْسِمُوهُ ، ثُمَّ ائْتُونِي بِهِ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ بِالسَّرِقَةِ وَالرُّجُوعِ عَنْهُ قَالَ عَطَاءٌ : إِذَا اعْتَرَفَ مَرَّةً قُطِعَ، غبر 17275/سنن نسائي، تَلْقِينُ السَّارِقِ، غمبر 4887)

وجه (۱) دليل ابي يوسف قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ \ رَأَيْتُ عَلِيًّا رضِي الله عنه أَقَرَّ عِنْدَهُ سَارِقٌ مَرَّتَيْنِ " فَقَطَعَ يَدَهُ، وَعَلَّقَهَا فِي عُنُقِهِ "، فَكَأَيِّ أَنْظُرُ إِلَى يَدِهِ تَضْرِبُ صَدْرَهُ، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَعْلِيقِ الْيَدِ فِي عُنُقِ السَّارِقِ ، نمبر 17274)

وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ أَنَّ يَعَلَى بْنَ أُمَيَّةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِعُمَرَ إِنَّا بِأَرْضِ فِيهَا شَرَابٌ كَثِيرٌ - يَعْنِي الْيَمَنَ - فَكَيْفَ تَجْلِدُهُ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَقْرِى أُمَّ الْقُرْآنِ فَلَمْ يَقْرَأْهَا، وَلَمْ يَعْرِفَ رِدَاءَهُ، إِذَا أَلْقَيْتَهُ بَيْنَ الْأَرْدِيَةِ فَاحْدُدْهُ، (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الريح، نمبر 17031)
It is established by the testimony of two witnesses. From Abu Huraira: A thief who stole a cloak was brought to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). They said: This one stole. He said: I do not think he stole. The man said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah, I stole. He said: Take him and cut off his hand, then cauterize it, then bring him to me. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on confession of theft and retraction; Sunan Nasa'i). Aspect (1) Proof of Abu Yusuf: The statement of a Companion for establishment: I saw Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when a thief confessed twice before him, so he cut off his hand and hung it around his neck, as if I see his hand striking his chest. (Sunan Bayhaqi). Aspect (2) Statement of a Tabi'i for establishment: that Ya'la ibn Umayyah said: I said to Umar: We are in a land where there is much drink - meaning Yemen - so how do you flog him? He said: If he recites the Mother of the Qur'an but does not read it, and does not recognize his garment when you throw it among the garments, then impose the hadd. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the commentary on Al-Quduri. It presents the Hanafi position that the hadd punishment (for drinking, by context) is established by the testimony of two male witnesses. The commentator provides three proofs: first, a hadith from Abu Huraira about a thief who confessed; though this appears to be about theft, it establishes the principle that a confession or testimony leads to punishment. Second, the action of Caliph Ali cutting off a thief's hand after two confessions. Third, a statement from Umar ibn al-Khattab regarding the flogging for drinking, indicating that the hadd is applied when the drinker fails to recite the Fatihah properly or recognize his garment, which implies the need for evidence. These proofs collectively support the rule that two witnesses are sufficient to establish a hadd punishment in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony in court; here specifically the testimony of two male witnesses to establish a hadd punishment.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By the testimony of two male witnesses

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the hadd for drinking is established only by the testimony of two male witnesses or a confession, reflecting the high evidentiary standard for fixed punishments.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

8 min
Women's Testimony in Hudud: The Hanafi Position
States the ruling and cites a sunna-based proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, identify the proof from the sunna, and explain the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
In hudud, women's testimony is rejected entirely — even alongside men.

This passage lays down a critical evidence rule in Hanafi fiqh: women's testimony has no place in hudud punishments. The ruling is not based on a general distrust of women, but on a specific legal tradition (sunna) transmitted from the Prophet and the early caliphs. Understanding this rule requires distinguishing between different areas of evidence law and recognizing the force of continuous practice as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the Arabic opening: 'وَلَا يُقْبَلُ فِيهِ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ'. The pronoun 'فِيهِ' refers back to hudud. So the ruling is specific to hudud cases only. Women's testimony is not accepted at all, even when accompanied by male witnesses.
The ruling does not extend to other areas like financial transactions or marriage.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a report from al-Zuhri, a Tabi'i, who says: 'مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ: أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الخُدُودِ'. This means the established practice (sunna) from the Prophet and the two caliphs (Abu Bakr and 'Umar) is that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud.
The statement is classified as a Sunnah ahad report, but its content is a continuous practice.
3
Understand the epistemological weight
The phrase 'مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ' indicates an ongoing, agreed-upon practice. For the Hanafi school, such a report—especially when supported by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs—is a strong proof. The thubut (transmission) is zanni, but the dalala (meaning) is clear and binding.
The report is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that women's testimony is accepted in hudud when accompanied by a male witness (i.e., one man + two women). Their proof includes the general verse on testimony (2:282) and analogy with other cases. The Hanafi response is that hudud require strict proof, and the sunna has specifically excluded women.
The practical difference: in Shafi'i, a hudud case can be proven with one man and two women; in Hanafi, it cannot.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
If a theft case comes before a Hanafi qadi with only female witnesses (even with men), the hadd cannot be imposed. In a Shafi'i court, it could be imposed if the witnesses meet their standard. This illustrates how methodological differences in accepting evidence directly affect outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْبَلُ فِيهِ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ
لا وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يُقْبَلُ فِيهِ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ: " مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ: أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الخُدُودِ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، نمبر 28714/مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ هَلْ تَجُوزُ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ فِي الحدُودِ وَغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 15402)
اصول : حد شرب میں شہادت سے رجوع کرلے تو حد بھی ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
اصول : حدود میں مردوں کیساتھ عورتوں کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔
And women's testimony along with men is not accepted in it. No aspect (1): Statement of the Tabi'i for the establishment that women's testimony is not accepted in it: from al-Zuhri, he said: The sunna from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and the two caliphs after him has passed that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Principles: In the hadd for drinking, if the witness retracts, the hadd is dropped. Principles: In hudud, the testimony of women along with men is not acceptable.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud punishments. The proof is from al-Zuhri, who reports a continuous practice (sunna) from the Prophet and the first two caliphs that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. This is a strong precedent. The commentary also adds two Urdu principles: first, if the witness(es) retract in the case of hadd for drinking, the punishment is dropped; second, the general principle that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and differs from other schools that allow women's testimony in some cases.

Key Terms
حدود (ḥudūd): Plural of hadd; fixed punishments for crimes like theft, drinking, adultery, false accusation.
شهادة النساء (shahādat al-nisā'): Testimony of women; in this context, women's testimony is not accepted in hudud cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof cited for the Hanafi ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud?
A) A Quranic verse explicitly stating so
B) A hadith from the Prophet that hudud are warded off by doubts
C) A report from al-Zuhri that the sunna from the Prophet and the two caliphs was that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud
D) Consensus of all companions

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony is not accepted in hudud because the established practice (sunna) from the Prophet and the first two caliphs excludes it, a ruling unique to the Hanafi school.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

The Hadd for False Accusation (Qadhf): Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on hadd al-qadhf with Quranic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) for free and slave persons, identify the conditions for the hadd, and cite the primary Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Eighty lashes for a free false accuser, forty for a slave — the Quran itself prescribes the measure.

This lesson examines the Islamic punishment for falsely accusing a chaste person of zina. The Quran explicitly sets the penalty at eighty lashes for free individuals, and the Hanafi school details the procedure, including the reduction for slaves. Understanding this ruling is key to appreciating how Islamic law protects honor and reputation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what qadhf is (false accusation of zina) and the prescribed punishment: 80 lashes for a free person, 40 for a slave.
The punishment is a hadd (fixed penalty) that is wajib upon the accuser when conditions are met.
2
Recognize the conditions for the hadd
List the conditions: the accused must be muhsan (free, Muslim, adult, chaste), the accusation must be explicit (sarih al-zina), and the accused must demand the punishment.
Implicit accusations (ta'rid) do not incur the hadd.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (Surah Nur 24:4) commands eighty lashes. In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation (wujub).
The verse also requires four witnesses for an accusation to be valid; without them, the accuser is punished.
4
Note the distinction between free and slave
The source cites the practice of Caliphs Umar and Uthman, who lashed a slave forty times for false accusation, based on the principle that the slave's punishment is half that of a free person.
This is consistent with other hudud where slaves receive half the punishment.
5
Understand procedural details
The lashes must be distributed over the body, avoiding the face and private parts. The accused is not stripped naked, but heavy clothing (e.g., fur) is removed.
These details ensure the punishment is effective without causing excessive harm or humiliation.

Source Text

بَابُ حَدَ الْقَذْفِ
رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - إِذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنَا أَوْ امْرَأَةَ مُحْصَنَةً بِصَرِيحِ الزِّنَا فَطَالَبَهُ الْمَقْذُوفُ بِالْحَدِ حَدَّهُ الْحَاكِمُ ثَمَانِينَ سَوْطًا إِنْ كَانَ حُرًّا لـ يُفَرَّقُ الضَّرْبُ عَلَى أَعْضَائِهِ وَلَا يُجَرَّدُ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ يُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ ، وَالْحَشْوُا فَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَاذِفُ عَبْدًا جُلِدَ أَرْبَعِينَ

وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت إِذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا \ عَنِ الْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَ: " مَا كُنَّا نَرَى الجُلْدَ إِلَّا فِي الْقَدْفِ الْبَيِّنِ وَالنَّفْي الْبَيِّنِ، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا حَدَّ إِلَّا فِي الْقَذْفِ الصَّريح، نمبر 17145 مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَاب التَّعْرِيضُ، نمبر 13703)

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ جَاءَهُ أَعْرَابِيٌّ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، إِنَّ امْرَأَتِي وَلَدَتْ غُلَامًا أَسْوَدَ، فَقَالَ: هَلْ لَكَ مِنْ
إبلالخ، (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّعْرِيض ، نمبر 6847/ مسلم ، كتاب اللعان،1500)

وجه (۳) الآية لثبوت إذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنَا \ ثَمَنِينَ جَلْدَةً وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةٌ أبداً (سورة النور ، 24 آيت نمبر 4)

لوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت يُفَرَّقُ الضَّرْبُ عَلَى أَعْضَائِهِ \ عَنْ عِكْرِمَةَ بْنِ خَالِدٍ قَالَ: أَتَى عَلِيًّا رَجُلٌ فِي حَدٍ فَقَالَ: «اضْرِبْ وَأَعْطِ كُلَّ عُضْوِ حَقَّهُ، وَاجْتَنِبْ وَجْهَهُ وَمَذَاكِيرَهُ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ ضَرْبِ الْخُدُودِ، وَهَلْ ضَرَبَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالسَّوْطِ، نمبر 13517)

وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَلَا يُجرَّدُ مِنْ ثِيَابِهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ يُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ \ سَأَلْتُ الْمُغِيرَةَ بْنَ شُعْبَةَ، عَنِ الْقَاذِفِ أَتُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ؟ قَالَ: «لَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فَرُوْا أَوْ تَحْشُوَّ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ وَضْعِ الرِّدَاءِ، نمبر 13526/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الزَّانِيَةِ وَالزَّانِي يُخْلَعُ عَنْهُمَا ثِيَابُهُمَا أَوْ يُضْرَبَانِ فِيهَا ، نمر 28327)
:
وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَ الْقَاذِفُ عَبْدًا جُلِدَ أَرْبَعِينَ افَقَالَ : أَدْرَكْتُ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ وَعُثْمَانَ بْنَ عَفَّانَ الله رضي عنهما وَاخْلَفَاءَ هَلُمَّ جَرَّا، مَا رَأَيْتُ أَحَدًا جَلَدَ عَبْدًا فِي فِرْيَةٍ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ الْعَبْدِ يَقْذِفُ حُرًّا، غبر (17139/)

اصول: کسی پاکدامن عورت یا مرد پر زنا کی تہمت لگانا مگر چار گواہ سے ثابت نہ کر سکے تو ایسے مدعی پر حد ہے۔
Chapter on the hadd for false accusation. He said: The chapter on the hadd for false accusation. May Allah have mercy on him: When a man accuses a muhsan man or a muhsan woman of clear zina, and the accused demands the hadd, the judge imposes eighty lashes if he is free, and the lashes are distributed over his limbs, and he is not stripped of his clothes except that his fur and padding are removed. If the accuser is a slave, he is lashed forty. Aspect (1) Statement of the Tabi'i for establishment: from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad: We did not consider lashing except in clear accusation and clear denial. (...). Aspect (2) Hadith for establishment: from Abu Huraira: A Bedouin came to the Prophet and said: My wife gave birth to a black son... (Bukhari, Muslim). Aspect (3) The verse for establishment: Eighty lashes and never accept their testimony (Surah Nur, 24:4). Aspect (1) Hadith for establishment: the lashes are distributed over his limbs: from Ikrimah: A man came to Ali regarding a hadd, so he said: Strike and give each limb its due, and avoid his face and private parts. Aspect (1) Statement of the Companion for establishment: He is not stripped of his clothes except that the fur is removed: I asked al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba about the accuser, whether his clothes are removed. He said: Nothing is removed except if there is a fur or padding. Aspect (1) Statement of the Companion for establishment that if the accuser is a slave, he is lashed forty: I witnessed Umar and Uthman; I never saw anyone lash a slave for false accusation more than forty. (Sunan Bayhaqi). Principle: Accusing a chaste man or woman of zina without four witnesses incurs the hadd on the accuser.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on hadd al-qadhf presents the Hanafi ruling in detail. The matn states that if a free person accuses a muhsan (chaste, free, Muslim adult) of explicit zina, and the accused demands the punishment, the judge imposes eighty lashes. The lashes are distributed over the body (not concentrated in one spot), and the accused is not stripped naked, but any thick clothing like fur or padding is removed to allow the lashes to reach the skin. If the accuser is a slave, the punishment is forty lashes. The commentary provides proofs: (1) a statement from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad that lashing is only for clear accusation; (2) the hadith of the Bedouin whose wife gave birth to a black child, indicating that accusing without proof leads to punishment; (3) the Quranic verse Surah Nur 24:4 which prescribes eighty lashes for false accusation; (4) the hadith from Ali about distributing lashes; (5) the report from al-Mughira about removing the fur; and (6) the practice of Umar and Uthman lashing a slave forty. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes: anyone who accuses a chaste man or woman of zina without four witnesses is subject to the hadd. This is a core ruling in Islamic criminal law.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): The act of falsely accusing a chaste person of zina (adultery or fornication).
محصن (muḥṣan): A person who is free, Muslim, adult, and chaste (not previously convicted of zina).
صريح الزنا (ṣarīḥ al-zinā): Explicit accusation of zina, as opposed to hinting or ta'riz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the punishment for a free person who falsely accuses a muhsan of zina?
A) Forty lashes
B) Eighty lashes
C) One hundred lashes
D) Stoning

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a free person who falsely accuses a muhsan of explicit zina without four witnesses is punished with eighty lashes, while a slave receives forty, based on the Quran and practice of the companions.
