The Definition of Ihsan and Its Conditions
Defining ihsan with its five conditions and supporting evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan as defined by the Hanafi school and explain why each is required.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, and chastity — all five are necessary for the hadd of qadhf.

In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) applies only when the accused is muhsan. But what exactly is ihsan? This lesson unpacks the five conditions that constitute ihsan as defined by Imam al-Quduri, with evidence from the early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
List the five qualities that the accused must possess to be considered muhsan: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (not having committed zina).
Memorize this list; it is the core of the definition.
2
Understand the rationale for each
Each condition ensures the legal capacity and dignity of the victim. For example, freedom ensures full legal personhood; chastity ensures the accusation actually harms honor.
Condition of chastity does not require marriage — simply abstaining from zina suffices.
3
Analyze the evidence from Ata
The source cites Ata: a man consummated a marriage that turned out to be with his foster-sister; Ata said that woman is not muhsan because the marriage was void and thus the consummation was zina, negating chastity.
This shows that void marriage does not establish ihsan.
4
Apply: who qualifies as muhsan?
Given a scenario, verify each condition. For instance, a free adult sane Muslim woman who never committed zina is muhsan; a slave or a woman who committed zina is not.
The hadd for qadhf is only obligatory if the victim is muhsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِحْصَانُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَقْذُوفُ حُرًّا بَالِغَا عَاقِلًا مُسْلِمًا عَفِيفًا عَنْ فِعْلَ الزَّنَا
وَمَنْ نَفَى نَسَبَ غَيْرِهِ فَقَالَ لَسْت لِأَبِيكَ أَوْيَا ابْنَ الزَّانِيَةِ وَأُمُّهُ مَيِّتَةٌ مُحْصَنَةٌ فَطَالَبَهُ الِابْنُ بِحَدِّهَا حُدَّ الْقَاذِفُ
وَلا يُطَالَبُ بِحَدِ الْقَذْفِ لِلْمَيِّتِ إلَّا مَنْ يَقَعُ الْقَدَحُ فِي نَسَبِهِ بِقَدْفِهِ
وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَقْذُوفُ مُحْصَنَا جَازَ لِابْنِهِ الْكَافِرِ، وَالْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ بِالحَدِ
وَلَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ مَوْلَاهُ بِقَدْفِ أُمِهِ الْحَرَّةِ الْمُسْلِمَةِ
فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَذْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَرَبِيَّ يَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَمْ يُحَدِّ
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالإِحْصَانُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَقْذُوفُ حُرًّا عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ تَزَوَّجَ بِامْرَأَةٍ ثُمَّ دَخَلَ بِمَا فَإِذَا هِيَ أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ بِإِحْصَانِ». وَقَالَهُ مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق ، بَابُ هَلْ يَكُونُ النِّكَاحُ الْفَاسِدُ إِحْصَانًا»نمبر 13305)
وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ نَفَى نَسَبَ غَيْرِهِ فَقَالَ لَسْت لِأَبِيكَ قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: لَا حَدَّ إِلَّا عَلَى رَجُلَيْنِ : رَجُلٌ قَذَفَ مُحْصَنَةً أَوْ نَفَى رَجُلًا مِنْ أَبِيهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أُمُّهُ أَمَةً،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْفِي الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ، نمبر 28241)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَقْذُوفُ مُحْصَنَا جَازَ لِابْنِهِ الْكَافِرِ سَأَلْتُ الزُّهْرِيَّ عَنْ رَجُلٍ نَفَى رَجُلًا مِنْ أَبِ لَهُ فِي الشِرْكِ، فَقَالَ: «عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لِأَنَّهُ نَفَاهُ مِنْ نَسَبِهِ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الرَّجُلِ يَنْفِي الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أبِ لَهُ في الشرك، نمبر 28885)
و وجه : (۱)قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ مَوْلَاهُ بِقَدْفِ أُمِّهِ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَقْذِفُ ابْنَهُ، قَالَ: «لَا يُجْلَدُ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الرَّجُلِ يَقْذِفُ ابْنَهُ مَا عَلَيْهِ، نمبر 28239/مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ الْأَبِ يَفْتَرِي عَلَى ابْنِهِ، نمبر 13806)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَذْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ: «لَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَذَفَ رَجُلًا فَعَفَا وَأَشْهَدَ ثُمَّ جَاءَ بِهِ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، أَخَذَ لَهُ بِحَقِّهِ وَلَوْ مَكَثَ ثَلَاثِينَ سَنَةً، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يُفْتَرَى عَلَيْهِ، مَا قَالُوا فِي عَفْوِهِ عَنْهُ، نمبر 28891)
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَرَي يَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَمْ يُعَدّاعَنِ الْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَ: مَا كُنَّا
And ihsan (chastity/guardianship) is that the accused is free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from the act of zina. And whoever negates the lineage of another and says 'You are not your father's [son]' or 'O son of the adulteress' while his mother is dead and muhsan, and the son demands her punishment, the accuser is punished. And punishment for qadhf regarding a deceased is not demanded except by the one whose lineage is affected by that qadhf. And if the accused is muhsan, it is permissible for his son who is a disbeliever and for the slave to demand the hadd. And it is not for a slave to demand [punishment] from his master for the qadhf of his Muslim free mother. Then if he confesses to the qadhf and then retracts, his retraction is not accepted. And whoever says to an Arab 'O Nabati', he is not punished. Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'ihsan is that the accused is free' – from Ata regarding a man who married a woman then consummated, and she turned out to be his foster-sister; he said: 'That is not ihsan.' And Ma'mar said it from Qatadah. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab hal yakunu al-nikah al-fasid ihsan, no. 13305). Evidence: Saying of a Companion for establishing 'whoever negates the lineage of another and says you are not your father's' – Abdullah said: 'There is no hadd except for two men: a man who accuses a muhsan woman or a man who negates a man from his father, even if his mother is a slave.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajuli yanfi al-rajula min abihi wa ummihi, no. 28241). Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'if the accused is muhsan, it is permissible for his son who is a disbeliever' – I asked al-Zuhri about a man who negated a man from his father in polytheism; he said: 'He is subject to the hadd because he negated him from his lineage.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajuli yanfi al-rajula min abihi lahu fi al-shirk, no. 28885). Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'it is not for a slave to demand from his master for qadhf of his mother' – from Ata regarding a man who accuses his son; he said: 'He is not flogged.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajuli yaqdhifu ibnahu ma 'alayh, no. 28239; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-abi yaftari 'ala ibnih, no. 13806). Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'if he confesses to qadhf and then retracts, his retraction is not accepted' – from al-Zuhri: 'If a man accuses a man, and he [the accuser] pardons and witnesses, then brings him to the imam after that, he takes his right even if thirty years pass.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajuli yuftara 'alayh, ma qalu fi 'afwihi 'anhu, no. 28891). Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'whoever says to an Arab O Nabati is not punished' – from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad: 'We were not...' (incomplete in OCR).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn defines ihsan (the condition of being muhsan) as having five qualities: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (not having committed zina). It then addresses negation of lineage as a form of qadhf. If someone says 'You are not your father's son' or 'O son of the adulteress' (when the mother is deceased and was muhsan), the son can demand the hadd punishment for his mother, because the slur affects his lineage. Only those whose lineage is directly impugned can demand punishment for a deceased person. Interestingly, if the accused is muhsan, even his non-Muslim son or a slave can demand the hadd on his behalf. However, a slave cannot demand punishment from his own master for slandering his free Muslim mother. Additionally, if the accuser confesses to qadhf and then retracts, the retraction is not accepted—the hadd must be carried out. Finally, calling an Arab 'O Nabati' (i.e., a non-Arab) is not considered qadhf and does not incur the hadd punishment, presumably because it does not amount to accusing of zina or negating lineage. The evidence from athar supports these rulings, showing the practical application by early authorities.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being muhsan: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (not having committed zina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Negation of Lineage as Qadhf
Rulings on negation of lineage as qadhf and related exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when someone negates another's lineage and identify who can demand punishment and when retraction is accepted.

Core Idea
Negating lineage is a form of qadhf because it implies the mother committed zina; the hadd applies with specific rules.

The source continues to address a specific form of qadhf: negating someone's lineage by saying 'You are not your father's son' or 'O son of the adulteress.' This lesson explores the nuanced rulings: who can demand hadd for a deceased mother, the role of a non-Muslim son or slave, and why a slave cannot demand against his master. Also, retraction of confession is not accepted, and calling an Arab 'Nabati' is not qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of negation of lineage
The act is saying something like 'You are not your father's son' or 'O son of the adulteress.' This implicitly accuses the mother of zina, thus constituting qadhf.
The key is that it necessarily impugns the mother's chastity.
2
Determine who can demand hadd for a deceased muhsan mother
Only the child whose lineage is affected can demand punishment. The text says: 'except the one whose lineage is affected by that qadhf.'
This protects the dignity of the deceased through the living heir.
3
Analyze exceptions: non-Muslim son and slave as claimants
If the accused is muhsan, even a non-Muslim son or a slave can demand hadd on his behalf. But a slave cannot demand against his own master for slandering his free Muslim mother.
The slave's right is limited due to the master's authority over him.
4
Note the irretractability of confession
If the accuser confesses to qadhf and then retracts, the retraction is not accepted. The hadd must be carried out.
This is based on the principle that confession is one of the strongest proofs.
5
Recognize what is not qadhf
Calling an Arab 'O Nabati' (a non-Arab) is not qadhf because it does not impute zina or negate lineage.
The insult must directly accuse of zina or negate lineage to be qadhf.

And ihsan (chastity/guardianship) is that the accused is free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from the act of zina. And whoever negates the lineage of another and says 'You are not your father's [son]' or 'O son of the adulteress' while his mother is dead and muhsan, and the son demands her punishment, the accuser is punished. And punishment for qadhf regarding a deceased is not demanded except by the one whose lineage is affected by that qadhf. Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn defines ihsan (the condition of being muhsan) as having five qualities: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste (not having committed zina). It then addresses negation of lineage as a form of qadhf. Additionally, if the accuser confesses to qadhf and then retracts, the retraction is not accepted—the hadd must be carried out. Finally, calling an Arab 'O Nabati' (i.e., a non-Arab) is not considered qadhf and does not incur the hadd punishment, presumably because it does not amount to accusing of zina or negating lineage. The evidence from athar supports these rulings, showing the practical application by early authorities.

Key Terms
نفي النسب (nafi al-nasab): Negating someone's lineage, e.g., saying 'You are not your father's son', which implies the mother committed zina, thus amounting to qadhf.

Two Specific Rulings in Qadhf: Retraction and Insults
Rulings on retracting confession and on specific insults not constituting qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retracting a confession in qadhf and identify which insults constitute qadhf.

Core Idea
A confession to qadhf cannot be retracted; not every insult is qadhf—only an explicit accusation of zina.

This lesson addresses two specific legal questions from the hudud of qadhf. When a person confesses to false accusation and then withdraws, does the hadd still apply? And is calling an Arab 'Nabati' punishable by the hadd of qadhf? The answers establish key principles about the binding nature of confession and the precise definition of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two rulings
Read the passage and identify the two distinct rulings: (1) retraction of qadhf confession is not accepted; (2) calling an Arab 'Nabati' does not incur hadd.
These are separate, independent rulings.
2
Analyse the rationale for retraction
In Hanafi fiqh, confession is a strong proof. Retraction is only accepted in the hadd of zina, not in qadhf, because the right of the victim (haqq adami) is involved. The confession triggers the hadd, and retraction cannot cancel it.
Compare with the rule for zina: confessor may retract before stoning.
3
Analyse the definition of qadhf
Qadhf requires an explicit or implicit accusation of zina. 'Nabati' is a general insult not implying zina, so it does not meet the legal definition. The hadd is not applied, but ta'zir may be.
The insult must clearly impute zina to qualify as qadhf.
4
Note the evidence
The passage cites sayings of tabi'in: al-Zuhri supports that retraction is not accepted even after pardon; al-Qasim supports that 'Nabati' is not qadhf.
These are not primary sources like Quran or hadith but are considered valid in Hanafi fiqh as precedents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَذْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَرَبِيَّ يَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَمْ يُحَدِّ
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَذْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ: «لَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَذَفَ رَجُلًا فَعَفَا وَأَشْهَدَ ثُمَّ جَاءَ بِهِ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، أَخَذَ لَهُ بِحَقِّهِ وَلَوْ مَكَثَ ثَلَاثِينَ سَنَةً، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يُفْتَرَى عَلَيْهِ، مَا قَالُوا فِي عَفْوِهِ عَنْهُ، نمبر 28891)
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَرَي يَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَمْ يُعَدّاعَنِ الْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَ: مَا كُنَّا
Then if he confesses to the qadhf and then retracts, his retraction is not accepted. And whoever says to an Arab 'O Nabati', he is not punished. Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'if he confesses to qadhf and then retracts, his retraction is not accepted' – from al-Zuhri: 'If a man accuses a man, and he [the accuser] pardons and witnesses, then brings him to the imam after that, he takes his right even if thirty years pass.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajuli yuftara 'alayh, ma qalu fi 'afwihi 'anhu, no. 28891). Evidence: Saying of a tabi'i for establishing 'whoever says to an Arab O Nabati is not punished' – from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad: 'We were not...'
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This short passage from Al-Quduri's matn gives two specific rulings. First, if a person confesses to qadhf (false accusation of zina) and then retracts the confession, the retraction is not accepted. The hadd punishment must still be applied. This is because confession is a strong proof, and retraction in hadd cases is only accepted for zina itself (if the confessor says he did not commit zina) but not for qadhf, perhaps because the right of the victim is involved. The evidence from al-Zuhri indicates that even if the accuser pardons and witnesses, the imam can still enforce the hadd because it is a right of Allah. Second, if someone calls an Arab 'O Nabati' (a term for a non-Arab, often used derogatorily), he is not subject to the hadd punishment for qadhf. This is because such an insult does not explicitly or implicitly accuse of zina; it is mere insult without the specific imputation required for qadhf. Both rulings are established by athar from the tabi'in.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession: the admission by the accuser that he committed qadhf.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction: withdrawing the confession after it has been made.
نبَطي (nabati): A term used to refer to non-Arabs, often pejoratively; here, it is not considered an accusation of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a common insult
B) Because it does not explicitly accuse of zina
C) Because the victim is an Arab
D) Because it is a term of endearment

Key Takeaway
Confession in qadhf is binding and retraction is ineffective; an insult like 'Nabati' does not meet the definition of qadhf.

The Rulings and Conditions of Qadhf (False Accusation)
Rulings and proofs for the hadd of qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ihsan for qadhf, identify which accusations incur the hadd, and apply the conditions to determine if qadhf is established.

Core Idea
Only explicit accusations of zina or lineage denial against a muhsan person incur the hadd of qadhf.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn lays down the foundational rules for the Islamic criminal punishment of false accusation (qadhf). It defines the crucial concept of ihsan (being muhsan) which determines when the hadd becomes obligatory. It also lists specific scenarios where the hadd applies or does not apply, supported by proofs from the Quran and the statements of the early generations. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the hadd penalty.

Guided Path
1
Define Ihsan for Qadhf
State the five conditions that make a person muhsan: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from zina. This is the foundation of the qadhf ruling.
Ihsan for qadhf differs slightly from ihsan for zina (which requires a valid marriage).
2
Identify Explicit Qadhf
Recognize the explicit words that constitute qadhf: accusing someone directly of zina (e.g., 'O son of the adulteress') or denying lineage (e.g., 'You are not your father's son').
The accusation must be clear and unambiguous (sarih).
3
Apply the Ihsan Condition
Check if the accused meets all five conditions of ihsan. If any condition is missing (e.g., the accused is a slave, non-Muslim, or has committed zina), the hadd is not incurred.
Note special cases: a slave can demand hadd for his muhsan parent, but a master accusing his slave's free mother is exempt.
4
Recognize Exceptions
Know which statements are not considered qadhf: calling an Arab 'Nabatean', 'son of the sky water', attributing to an uncle, etc. These do not clearly accuse zina or deny lineage.
These are ta'zir offenses at most, not hadd.
5
Understand the Proofs
Connect the rulings to the Quranic verse (24:4) which commands flogging for accusing muhsanat without witnesses. Also note the early authorities' sayings that reinforce the definition of ihsan.
The imperatives in the Quran indicate obligation (wujub).

Source Text

باب حد القذف
والإحصان أن يكون المقذوف حرا بالغا عاقلا مسلما عفيفا عن فعل الزنا
ومن نفى نسب غيره فقال لست لأبيك أو يا ابن الزانية وأمه ميتة محصنة فطالبه الابن بحدها حد القاذف
وإن كان المقذوف محصنا جاز لابنه الكافر، والعبد أن يطالب بالحد
وليس للعبد أن يطالب مولاه بقذف أمه الحرة المسلمة
فإن أقر بالقذف ثم رجع لم يقبل رجوعه
ومن قال لعربي يا نبطي لم يحد
ومن قال لرجل يا ابن ماء السماء فليس بقاذف
وإن نسبه إلى عمه أو إلى خاله أو زوج أمه فليس بقاذف
ومن وطئ وطأ حراما في غير ملكه لم يحد قاذفه
والملاعنة بولد لا يحد قاذفها
د وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالإِحْصَانُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَقْذُوفُ حُرًّا عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ تَزَوَّجَ بِامْرَأَةٍ ثُمَّ دَخَلَ بِمَا فَإِذَا هِيَ أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ بِإِحْصَانِ». وَقَالَهُ مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ هَلْ يَكُونُ النِّكَاحُ الْفَاسِدُ إِحْصَانًا»نمبر 13305)
د وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ نَفَى نَسَبَ غَيْرِهِ فَقَالَ لَسْت لِأَبِيكَ قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: " لَا حَدَّ إِلَّا عَلَى رَجُلَيْنِ : رَجُلٌ قَذَفَ مُحْصَنَةً أَوْ نَفَى رَجُلًا مِنْ أَبِيهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أُمُّهُ أَمَةً،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْفِي الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ، نمبر 28241)
د وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَقْذُوفُ مُحْصَنَا جَازَ لِابْنِهِ الْكَافِرِ سَأَلْتُ الزُّهْرِيَّ عَنْ رَجُلٍ نَفَى رَجُلًا مِنْ أَبِ لَهُ فِي الشِرْكِ، فَقَالَ: «عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لِأَنَّهُ نَفَاهُ مِنْ نَسَبِهِ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الرَّجُلِ يَنْفِي الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أبِ لَهُ في الشرك، نمبر 28885)
و وجه : (۱)قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِلْعَبْدِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَ مَوْلَاهُ بِقَذْفِ أُمِّهِ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَقْذِفُ ابْنَهُ، قَالَ: «لَا يُجْلَدُ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الرَّجُلِ يَقْذِفُ ابْنَهُ مَا عَلَيْهِ، نمبر 28239/مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ الْأَبِ يَفْتَرِي عَلَى ابْنِهِ، نمبر 13806)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِالْقَذْفِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ رُجُوعُهُ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ: «لَوْ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَذَفَ رَجُلًا فَعَفَا وَأَشْهَدَ ثُمَّ جَاءَ بِهِ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، أَخَذَ لَهُ بِحَقِّهِ وَلَوْ مَكَثَ ثَلَاثِينَ سَنَةً، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يُفْتَرَى عَلَيْهِ، مَا قَالُوا فِي عَفْوِهِ عَنْهُ، نمبر 28891)
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَرَبِيٍّ يَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَمْ يُحَدَّ عَنِ الْقَاسِمِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَ: مَا كُنَّا
اصول : ماں زندہ ہو اور ماں پر تہمت لگی تو ماں ہی کو حق مطالبہ ہے ماں کی حیات میں بیٹے کا مطالبہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔
نرى الجلد إلا في القذف البين والنفي البين، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا حَدَّ إِلَّا فِي الْقَذْفِ الصريح، نمبر 17145)
وجه : (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت إذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلٍ قَالَ لِرَجُلٍ عَرَبِيَّ: يَا نَبَطِيُّ، قَالُ: كُلُّنَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَيْسَ فِي هَذَا حَدٌ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ الْقَوْلُ سِوَى الْفِرْيَةِ، نمبر 13737)
وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ نَسَبَهُ إِلَى عَمِهِ أَوْ إِلَى خَالِهِ قَالُوا نَعْبُدُ إِلَهَكَ وَإِلَهَ آبَائِكَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ وَإِسْحَاقَ إِلَهًا وَاحِدًا وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت، نمبر 133)
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَدًا وَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْفَاسِقُونَ (سورة النور، 24 آية نمبر 4)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ، أَنَّهُ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ يَهُودِيَّةً أَوْ نَصْرَانِيَّةً، فَسَأَلَ النَّبِيَّ الله عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَنَهَاهُ عَنْهَا، وَقَالَ: «إِنَّهَا لَا تُحْصِنُكَ»،(سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ الْحُدُودِ وَالدِّيَاتِ وَغَيْرُهُ، نمبر 3297/سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنِ، نمبر 16941)
وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ تَزَوَّجَ بِامْرَأَةٍ، ثُمَّ دَخَلَ بِمَا فَإِذَا هِيَ أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ بِإِحْصَانِ». وَقَالَهُ مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ هَلْ يَكُونُ النِّكَاحُ الْفَاسِدُ إِحْصَانًا»نمبر 13305)
اصول: غیر محصن مرد و عورت پر تہمت لگانے سے حد قذف لازم نہیں ہو گی، بلکہ محصن ہونا ضروری ہے۔
اصول: زنا کی علامت موجود ہو اور عورت غیر محصن ہو تو اس پر تہمت لگانے پر حد قذف نہیں لگے گی۔
Chapter of the punishment for false accusation (qadhf). And al-ihsan is that the accused be free, adult, sane, Muslim, chaste from the act of zina. And whoever denies the lineage of another and says 'You are not your father's son' or 'O son of the adulteress' while his mother is a deceased muhsanah, and the son demands her hadd, the accuser is punished. And if the accused is muhsan, it is permissible for his son, even if a disbeliever, and the slave to demand the hadd. And it is not for the slave to demand from his master for accusing his free Muslim mother. If he confesses to qadhf then retracts, his retraction is not accepted. And whoever says to an Arab 'O Nabatean' is not punished. And whoever says to a man 'O son of the sky water' is not an accuser. And if he attributes him to his paternal uncle, or to his maternal uncle, or to his mother's husband, he is not an accuser. And whoever commits a forbidden intercourse not in his ownership, his accuser is not punished. And the woman who is lianed with a child, her accuser is not punished. Evidence: (1) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'Ihsan is that the accused be free...' from 'Ata regarding a man who married a woman and then had intercourse with her and she turned out to be his foster sister, he said: 'It is not ihsan.' And Ma'mar said it from Qatadah. (1) Saying of the Companion: 'And whoever denies another's lineage...' 'Abd Allah said: 'There is no hadd except on two men: a man who accused a muhsanah or denied a man from his father, even if his mother was a slave woman.' (1) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'And if the accused is muhsan, it is permissible for his disbeliever son...' I asked al-Zuhri about a man who denied a man from his father while in shirk, he said: 'The hadd is upon him because he denied him from his lineage.' (1) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'And it is not for the slave to demand from his master for accusing his mother...' from 'Ata regarding a man who accuses his son, he said: 'He is not flogged.' (1) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'If he confesses to qadhf then retracts...' from al-Zuhri: 'If a man accused a man, then forgave and had witnesses, then brought him to the imam after that, he takes his right even if thirty years passed.' (1) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'And whoever says to an Arab 'O Nabatean' is not punished...' from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad: 'We were not...' Principle: When the mother is alive and the accusation is against her, the mother has the right to demand [the hadd]; during the mother's life, the son's demand is not considered. We only see flogging in explicit qadhf and explicit denial. (2) Saying of the Tabi'i: 'When a man accuses a muhsan man...' from al-Sha'bi: 'All of us are Nabateans, there is no hadd in this.' (1) The verse for evidence: 'And if he attributes him to his paternal uncle...' They said: 'We worship your God and the God of your fathers, Ibrahim, Isma'il, and Ishaq, one God, and we are Muslims to Him' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:133). (1) The verse for evidence: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the transgressors' (Surah al-Nur, 24:4). (2) Hadith for evidence: from Ka'b ibn Malik that he wanted to marry a Jewish or Christian woman, so he asked the Prophet ﷺ, and he forbade him and said: 'She will not make you muhsan.' (3) Saying of the Tabi'i: from 'Ata regarding a man who married a woman... [same as earlier]. Principles: Accusing a non-muhsan man or woman does not necessitate the hadd of qadhf; rather, being muhsan is necessary. Principle: If a sign of zina is present and the woman is non-muhsan, then accusing her does not incur the hadd of qadhf.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the punishment for false accusation (qadhf) in al-Quduri's matn, accompanied by its proofs from the early generations. The text first defines 'ihsan' (the condition that makes one muhsan) for the victim: the accused must be free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from zina. This is a legal definition establishing when the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes) becomes obligatory. The proofs cite sayings of tabi'un like 'Ata and Qatadah that a woman married under a void contract or discovered to be a foster sister is not considered muhsan, so accusing her does not incur hadd.

The passage then lists specific cases of qadhf. Denying someone's lineage explicitly (e.g., 'You are not your son' or 'O son of an adulteress') is a form of qadhf, and if the deceased mother was muhsan, the son can demand the hadd. A disbeliever son or a slave can demand hadd for a muhsan parent, but a slave cannot demand hadd from his master for accusing his free Muslim mother. This is based on the principle that the master's authority overrides the slave's right. Confession to qadhf followed by retraction is not accepted, as the hadd is a right of Allah that, once established by confession, cannot be revoked.

Certain insults are not considered qadhf: calling an Arab 'Nabatean', calling someone 'son of the sky water' (i.e., illegitimate), or attributing someone to his uncle or mother's husband do not explicitly accuse zina or deny lineage in a legally actionable manner. The proofs include sayings of al-Sha'bi and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad. Also, accusers of those who committed haram intercourse (zina) or a woman lianed with a child are not punished because the accused are not muhsan. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur 24:4) requires the victim to be muhsan (chaste). The hadith from Ka'b ibn Malik shows that marrying a non-Muslim does not confer ihsan. The Urdu principles summarize: the hadd applies only when the accused is muhsan, and signs of zina or non-muhsan status remove the hadd.

Key Terms
القذف (al-qadhf): The act of accusing a chaste person of zina or denying their lineage explicitly, which incurs a hadd punishment.
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The condition of being muhsan: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from zina.
محصن (muhsan): A person who meets the conditions of ihsan: free, adult, sane, Muslim, and chaste from zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, which of the following accusations incurs the hadd of qadhf?
A) Calling a free Muslim adult who is chaste 'O son of the adulteress'
B) Calling an Arab 'O Nabatean'
C) Accusing a woman who committed zina with clear evidence of being an adulteress
D) Saying to someone 'You are your mother's son'

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf applies strictly to explicit accusations of zina or lineage denial against a muhsan person; otherwise, no hadd.

intermediate

Implicit Accusations Are Not Qadhf
Defines which statements do not constitute legal qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which statements constitute legal qadhf in Hanafi law and explain why implicit accusations do not trigger the hadd.

Core Idea
Only explicit false accusation of zina incurs the hadd; indirect insults about lineage are not punishable.

The hadd of qadhf protects the honor of muhsan individuals, but it applies only when the accusation is explicit. In this passage, al-Quduri clarifies that certain indirect expressions—like attributing someone to a relative other than his father or using metaphors—do not incur the hadd. Two proofs anchor this ruling: a Quranic verse and a statement of the tabi'i al-Sha'bi. Understanding the boundary between explicit and implicit is crucial for correctly applying this penal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the speaker says and whether the law considers it qadhf. The matn lists three examples: calling someone 'son of the sky's water' (implying illegitimacy), attributing him to his uncle, maternal uncle, or mother's husband. In all cases, the speaker is not a qadif.
The ruling is negative: these acts do not trigger the hadd.
2
Recognize the conditions for hadd
For the hadd of qadhf to apply, the accusation must be explicit (sariḥ) and the victim must be muhsan. Implicit or allusive statements (kināyah) do not suffice. This is the core Hanafi rule.
Other schools may consider some kināyah as sufficient if the intent is clear.
3
Examine the first proof: Quranic verse
The verse (2:133) shows the sons of Ya'qub attributing Abraham to his 'āba' (fathers), which includes paternal uncles. This indicates that attributing someone to a paternal uncle is not a false lineage claim, thus not qadhf.
The term 'aba' is broad; the Quran uses it permissively.
4
Examine the second proof: saying of al-Sha'bi
Al-Sha'bi ruled that calling a Bedouin 'Nabaṭī' (non-Arab) does not incur hadd because it is not an explicit accusation of zina. This precedent from a major tabi'i reinforces the requirement of explicitness.
The athar is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
5
Apply the Hanafi principle and note ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is that the ḥadd is only for sariḥ qadhf. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may include certain implicit statements. The practical difference: under Hanafi law, these insults result at most in ta'zir, not hadd.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the type of punishment (ḥadd vs. ta'zīr).

Source Text

بَابُ حَدِ الْقَذْف
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِرَجُلٍ يَا ابْنَ مَاءِ السَّمَاءِ فَلَيْسَ بِقَاذِفٍ وَإِنْ نَسَبَهُ إِلَى عَمِّهِ أَوْ إِلَى خَالِهِ أَوْ زَوْجِ أُمِّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِقَاذِفِ
(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا حَدَّ إِلَّا فِي الْقَذْفِ الصريح، نمبر 17145)
وجه : (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت إذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا \ عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ رَجُلٍ قَالَ لِرَجُلٍ عَرَبِيَّ: يَا نَبَطِيُّ، قَالُ: كُلُّنَا نَبَطِيٌّ لَيْسَ فِي هَذَا حَدٌ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابٌ الْقَوْلُ سِوَى الْفِرْيَةِ، نمبر 13737)
وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَإِنْ نَسَبَهُ إِلَى عَمِهِ أَوْ إِلَى خَالِهِ قَالُوا نَعْبُدُ إِلَهَكَ وَإِلَهَ عَابَابِكَ إبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ وَإِسْحَاقَ إِلَهَا وَاحِدًا وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ (سورة البقرة، 2 آية، نمبر 133)
The chapter of the hadd of qadhf. And whoever says to a man 'O son of the water of the sky' is not a slanderer. And if he attributes him to his uncle or his maternal uncle or his mother's husband, he is not a slanderer. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Whoever said: No hadd except in explicit qadhf, no. 17145) Proof: (2) Saying of the follower for evidence: When a man accuses a man who is muhsan... from al-Sha'bi that he was asked about a man who said to a Bedouin man 'O Nabati', he said: 'We are all Nabati; there is no hadd in this.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter: The saying other than slander, no. 13737) Proof: (1) The verse for evidence: 'And when he attributed him to his uncle or his maternal uncle, they said: We worship your God and the God of your fathers Ibrahim, Ismail, and Ishaq, one God, and we are Muslims to Him.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:133)
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri followed by two proofs (wajh) that serve as commentary. The ruling establishes that certain words and expressions do not constitute legal qadhf (false accusation of zina) even if uttered with intent to insult. The first example is calling someone 'O son of the water of the sky' meaning rain, which implies illegitimacy but is not explicit. The second example is attributing someone to a relative other than the father (uncle, maternal uncle, mother's husband), which is not a direct claim of illegitimate birth. The proofs support this: the first from a saying of al-Sha'bi that calling someone 'Nabati' (non-Arab) does not incur hadd because it is not explicit qadhf. The second proof cites the Quranic verse where the sons of Ya'qub attribute Abraham to his 'fathers' (using a broad term), showing that attribution to other than the biological father is permissible in language and not considered qadhf. The Hanafi position is clear: for the hadd of qadhf to be imposed, the accusation must be explicit and unambiguous. Implicit or indirect statements do not trigger the punishment.

Key Terms
قاذف (qadzif): One who makes a false accusation of zina (qadhf) against a muhsan person, liable to the hadd punishment.
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has had valid consummated marriage; accusation against such a person triggers the hadd of qadhf.
صريح (sariḥ): Explicit, unambiguous language. In qadhf, only sariḥ accusations (e.g., 'you committed zina') incur hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone says to another 'You are the son of the water of the sky', does the speaker become liable to the hadd of qadhf?
A) Yes, because it implies illegitimacy.
B) Yes, if the listener feels insulted.
C) No, because the statement is not an explicit accusation of zina.
D) No, because the listener is not muhsan.

Key Takeaway
Implicit insults about lineage do not incur the hadd of qadhf; only explicit false accusation of zina does.

When the Hadd of Qadhf Does Not Apply
Lists exceptions to the hadd of qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of ihsan for the hadd of qadhf and identify two scenarios where the accuser is not subject to hadd.

Core Idea
The hadd of qadhf only applies if the accused is muhsan.

The hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina) is a severe punishment, but it is not triggered by every accusation. The Qur'an limits it to cases where the accused is muhsan (chaste, free, adult, Muslim, and previously married). This lesson examines two important exceptions from al-Quduri's matn: accusing someone who actually committed zina, and accusing a woman who has been divorced by li'an (mula'anah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
Read the opening statement: 'Whoever has unlawful intercourse outside his ownership, his accuser is not hadded.' This is a clear ruling that the hadd of qadhf is lifted when the accused is a known fornicator.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and represents the relied-upon Hanafi position.
2
Understand the condition of ihsan
The key condition for the hadd of qadhf is that the accused must be muhsan. In Hanafi fiqh, muhsan means free, adult, Muslim, and having had valid consummated marriage. If any element is missing, the hadd does not apply.
Other madhahib may define ihsan differently (e.g., no Islam condition).
3
Examine the first case: accusing a zani
If a person commits zina, they lose the status of ihsan. Therefore, accusing them of zina—even if the accuser cannot produce four witnesses—does not incur the hadd of qadhf.
This does not mean the accusation is permissible; ta'zir may still apply.
4
Examine the second case: the mula'anah
A woman who has been divorced through li'an (mutual cursing) is no longer considered muhsan. Her husband's accusation and the li'an process remove her ihsan. Thus, a third party accusing her of zina after the li'an is not subject to hadd.
The child born from that marriage is attributed to the husband, but the woman's ihsan is not restored.
5
Analyze the proofs
The passage cites three proofs: the Qur'anic verse (24:4) which specifies 'al-muhsanat' (chaste women), a hadith showing a non-Muslim woman does not confer ihsan, and a saying of 'Ata' that an invalid marriage (foster sister) does not create ihsan. These all support the condition of ihsan.
The verse implies that accusing a non-muhsan is outside the scope of the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ قَاذِفُهُ وَالْمُلَاعَنَةُ بِوَلَدٍ لَا يُحَدُّ قَاذِفُهَا نَرَى الْجُلْدَ إِلَّا فِي الْقَذْفِ الْبَيِّنِ وَالنَّفْيِ الْبَيِّنِ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْنَا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ \ وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُواْ بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَنِينَ جَلْدَةً وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَدَةً أَبَداً وَأُوْلَيكَ هُمُ الْفَسِقُونَ (سورة النور ، 24 آية نمبر 4)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْنَا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ اعَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ ، أَنَّهُ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ يَهُودِيَّةً أَوْ نَصْرَانِيَّةً ، فَسَأَلَ النَّبي الله عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَنَهَاهُ عَنْهَا ، وَقَالَ: «إِنَّهَا لَا تُحْصِنُكَ»،(سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ الْخُدُودِ وَالدِّيَاتِ وَغَيْرُهُ ، نمبر 3297/سنن بيهقي ،بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: مَنْ أَشْرَكَ بِاللَّهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَنِ، نمبر 16941)
وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ وَطِئَ وَطْئًا حَرَامًا فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكِهِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ اعَنْ عَطَاءٍ فِي رَجُلٍ تَزَوَّجَ بِامْرَأَةِ، ثُمَّ دَخَلَ بِمَا فَإِذَا هِيَ أُخْتُهُ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ بِإِحْصَانِ». وَقَالَهُ مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق ، بَابُ هَلْ يَكُونُ النِّكَاحُ الْفَاسِدُ إِحْصَانًا»نمبر 13305)
اصول: غیر محصن مردو عورت پر تہمت لگانے سے حد قذف لازم نہیں ہو گی، بلکہ محصن ہوناضروری ہے۔ اصول : زنا کی علامت موجود ہو اور عورت غیر محصن ہو تو اس پر تہمت لگانے پر حد قذف نہیں لگے گی۔
And whoever has unlawful intercourse outside his ownership, his accuser is not hadded. And the mula'anah (woman cursed by li'an) with a child, her accuser is not hadded. We see lashing except in clear qadhf and clear denial. Proof: (1) The verse for evidence: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, lash them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the transgressors.' (Surah an-Nur 24:4) Proof: (2) The hadith for evidence: ... from Ka'b ibn Malik that he wanted to marry a Jewish or Christian woman, he asked the Prophet (PBUH) and he forbade him, saying: 'She does not make you muhsan.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 3297) Proof: (3) Saying of the follower for evidence: ... from 'Ata regarding a man who married a woman and then consummated, and it turned out she was his foster sister; he said: 'This is not ihsan.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 13305) Principle: Accusing a non-muhsan man or woman does not require the hadd of qadhf; rather, being muhsan is necessary. Principle: If the sign of zina exists and the woman is non-muhsan, then accusing her does not incur the hadd of qadhf.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri followed by proofs and a Urdu commentary. The ruling covers two cases: (1) If someone commits zina (unlawful intercourse) without being in a valid ownership (i.e., zina itself), then the person who accuses him of that zina is not subject to the hadd of qadhf. (2) A mula'anah (a woman who has been divorced by li'an, mutual curse) who has a child from that marriage: if someone accuses her of zina, the accuser is not hadded. The passage then adds a general principle: 'We see lashing (as punishment) except in clear qadhf and clear denial.' This means that in general, the punishment for false accusations is lashing, but it is only applied in cases of clear, explicit qadhf or clear denial (nafi bayyin). The proofs include the Qur'anic verse (Surah an-Nur 24:4) which establishes the hadd for false accusation of muhsan women, but by implication, if the accuser is not muhsan, the hadd is not applied. The hadith from Ka'b ibn Malik shows that a non-Muslim woman does not make a man muhsan, so accusing her does not trigger the hadd. The saying of 'Ata' establishes that a marriage that is invalid (like foster sister) does not constitute ihsan. The Urdu commentary summarizes: accusing a non-muhsan (male or female) does not require the hadd of qadhf; being muhsan is necessary for the hadd to apply.

Key Terms
ملاعنة (mula'anah): A woman who has been divorced through li'an (mutual cursing) after being accused of zina by her husband; she is considered non-muhsan for the purpose of qadhf from third parties.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being muhsan: free, adult, Muslim, and having had a valid consummated marriage. Essential for the hadd of qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because she is not a Muslim.
B) Because she is not considered muhsan after the li'an.
C) Because the accuser is a relative.
D) Because the child proves she is not guilty.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf is conditional upon the accused being muhsan; accusing a non-muhsan does not trigger the fixed punishment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Hadd vs Ta'zir for Accusations of Zina and Insults
Specifies punishments for different types of accusations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a sharia accusation warrants hadd (fixed punishment) versus ta'zir (discretionary punishment), and state the Hanafi limits of ta'zir.

Core Idea
Only accusing a muhsan of zina gets hadd; all other false accusations receive ta'zir or no penalty.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar lays out a critical distinction in Islamic penal law: the fixed punishment (hadd) for false accusations of zina (qadhf) is reserved for cases where the accused is muhsan (free and chaste). When the accused is a slave, a non-Muslim, or when the allegation is not zina but a mere insult, the punishment shifts to ta'zir (discretionary flogging) or sometimes nothing at all. We will walk through these categories, examine the proofs from the Companions and Followers, and understand the Hanafi limits on ta'zir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Accusation Categories
The passage distinguishes between accusing a muhsan of zina versus accusing a non-muhsan (slave, umm walad, non-Muslim) of zina, and also accusations of non-zina insults like 'fasiq' or 'khabith'.
Muhsan is a free, adult, chaste Muslim.
2
Determine the Punishment for Each Category
For accusing a muhsan of zina: hadd (80 lashes). For accusing a non-muhsan of zina or a Muslim of non-zina insult: ta'zir (3-39 lashes). For insults like 'donkey' or 'pig': no ta'zir (but may be subject to a ruler's discretion).
The mula'anah (li'an wife) without child is considered muhsan, so her accuser receives hadd.
3
Understand the Condition of Muhsan
The underlying principle is that hadd applies only if the accused would receive hadd if guilty of zina themselves. Slaves and non-Muslims are not muhsan, so they cannot be witnesses for hadd, and accusations against them do not trigger hadd.
This is the key 'illa (effective cause) for the ruling.
4
Examine the Proofs
The text cites sayings of Ali and tabi'un (al-Zuhri, Qatada, Ibrahim) to confirm that such accusations lead to ta'zir or no hadd. The proof for ta'zir limits comes from al-Sha'bi (maximum 40) but the matn sets 39 to keep it less than the hadd of 80.
Qawl Sahabi (Ali) and Qawl Tabi'i are the source of the ruling.
5
Apply the Ta'zir Rules
The Hanafi school fixes ta'zir between 3 and 39 lashes. This is to ensure it remains a lesser penalty than hadd. The judge has discretion within this range based on the severity of the accusation.
The minimum is three lashes; maximum is one less than the lowest hadd (80 for zina).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت الملاعن بغير ولد حدقاذفا وَمَنْ قَذَفَ أَمَةً أَوْ عَبْدًا أَوْ أُمَّ وَلَدٍ أَوْ كَافِرًا بِالزِّنَا أَوْ قَذَفَ مُسْلِمًا بِغَيْرِ الزِّنَا فَقَالَ: يَا فَاسِقُ أَوْ يَا خَبِيثُ عُزِّرَ
وَإِنْ قَالَ يَا حِمَارُ يَا خِنْزِيرُ لَمْ يُعَزَّرْ وَالتَّعْزِيرُ أَكْثَرُهُ تِسْعَةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ سَوْطًا وَأَقَلُّهُ ثَلَاثُ جَلَدَاتٍ
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وان كانت الملاعن بغير ولد حدقاذفا اعَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، وَقَتَادَةَ قَالَ: «مَنْ قَذَفَ الْمُلَاعِنَةَ جُلدَ الْحَدَّ، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَاب الْقَوْلُ سِوَى الْفِرْيَةِ، نمبر 12463/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي قَاذِفِ الْمُلَاعَنَةِ أَوِ ابْنِهَا، نمبر 28470)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ قَذَفَ أَمَةً أَوْ عَبْدًا \ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ افْتَرَى عَلَى عَبْدٍ، أَوْ أَمَةٍ قَالَ: «يُعَزِّرُ ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ فِرْيَةِ الْحُرِ عَلَى الْمَمْلُوكِ، غبر 13797 / مصنف ابن ابي شيبه مَا قَالُوا فِي قَاذِفِ أُمِّ الْوَلَدِ، نمبر 28248)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ قَذَفَ أَمَةً أَوْ عَبْدًا \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ أَنَّهُ، قَالَ: «مَنْ قَذَفَ يَهُودِيًّا أَوْ نَصْرَانِيَّا، فَلَا حَدَّ عَلَيْهِ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الْمُسْلِمِ يَقْذِفُ الدِّمِّيَّ عَلَيْهِ حَدٌ أَمْ لا، نمبر 28204/مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْفِرْيَةِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ،نمبر13782)
وجه (۳)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ قَذَفَ أَمَةً أَوْ عَبْدًا \ قَالَ عَلِيٌّ قَوْلُ الرَّجُلِ لِلرَّجُلِ: يَا خَبِيثُ يَا فَاسِقُ، قَالَ: «هُنَّ فَوَاحِشُ، وَفِيهِنَّ عُقُوبَةٌ وَلَا تَقُوهُنَّ فَتَعَوَّدَهُنَّ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الرَّجُل يَقُولُ لِلرَّجُلُ: يَا خَبِيثُ يَا فَاسِقُ، غبر 28964/)
وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ يَا حِمَارُ يَا خِنْزِيرُ لَمْ يُعَزَّرًا سَمِعْتُ عَلِيًّا له يَقُولُ : " إِنَّكُمْ سَأَلْتُمُونِي عَنِ الرَّجُلِ يَقُولُ لِلرَّجُلِ : يَا كَافِرُ يَا فَاسِقُ يَا حِمَارُ، وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ حَدٌ، وَإِنَّمَا فِيهِ عُقُوبَةٌ مِنَ السُّلْطَانِ، فَلَا تَعُودُوا فَتَقُولُوا، (سنن بيهقى بَابُ مَاجَاءَ فِي الشَّتْم دُونَ الْقَدْفِ، غبر 17150)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَالتَّعْزِيرُ أَكْثَرُهُ تِسْعَةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ سَوْطًا \ عَنِ الشَّعْبِي، قَالَ: «التَّعْزِيرُ مَا بَيْنَ السَّوْطِ إِلَى الْأَرْبَعِينَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي التَّعْزِيرِ كَمْ هُوَ وَكَمْ يَبْلُغُ بِهِ، نمبر 28872)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت إذَا قَذَفَ الرَّجُلُ رَجُلًا مُحْصَنًا \ عَنِ الصَّحَاكِ، قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم:
اصول : حد کے لئے لازم ہے کہ آدمی محصن ہو اور محسن نہ ہو تو حد نہیں البتہ تعزیر ہو گی لہذا غلام ، باندی اور کا فریر تہمت لگانے والے کو حد نہیں بلکہ تعزیر ہو گی کیونکہ یہ محسن نہیں ہیں۔
And if the mula'anah is without a child, her accuser is hadded. And whoever accuses a female slave or a male slave or a umm walad or a non-Muslim of zina, or accuses a Muslim of other than zina, saying 'O sinner' or 'O wicked one', he is subjected to ta'zir. And if he says 'O donkey' or 'O pig', he is not subjected to ta'zir. And the ta'zir, its maximum is thirty-nine lashes and its minimum is three stripes. Proof: (1) Saying of the follower for evidence: ... from al-Zuhri and Qatada said: 'Whoever accuses the mula'anah is flogged with the hadd.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 12463) Proof: (1) Saying of the follower for evidence: ... from al-Zuhri regarding a man who slandered a slave or female slave, he said: 'He is given ta'zir.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 13797) Proof: (2) Saying of the follower for evidence: ... from Ibrahim that he said: 'Whoever accuses a Jew or Christian, there is no hadd upon him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 28204) Proof: (3) Saying of the companion for evidence: ... Ali said: 'A man's saying to a man: O wicked, O sinner, they are obscenities, and in them is a punishment, so do not utter them lest you become accustomed.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 28964) Proof: (1) Saying of the companion for evidence: ... I heard Ali say: 'You asked me about a man saying to another: O disbeliever, O sinner, O donkey; there is no hadd in it, rather there is a punishment from the ruler, so do not return to saying them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 17150) Proof: (1) Saying of the follower for evidence: ... from al-Sha'bi said: 'Ta'zir is between the (single) lash and forty.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 28872) Proof: (2) Hadith for evidence: ... from al-Dahhak said: The Prophet (PBUH) said: ... Principle: For hadd, it is necessary that the person be muhsan; if he is not muhsan, then there is no hadd, but rather ta'zir is given. So the one who accuses a slave, a female slave, or a non-Muslim, there is no hadd for them, but ta'zir, because they are not muhsan.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage contains a series of rulings from the matn of al-Quduri with proofs and a concluding Urdu commentary. First, it distinguishes the case of the mula'anah: if she has no child, the accuser is subject to the hadd (80 lashes), unlike the previous case where she has a child (no hadd). This shows that the child from li'an makes her non-muhsan; without child, if the li'an was on the basis of a false accusation, the accuser may be hadded. Second, it rules on accusations against those who are not muhsan: slaves, female slaves, umm walad, and non-Muslims: accusing them of zina does not incur the hadd but instead ta'zir (discretionary punishment). Third, accusing a Muslim of something other than zina (e.g., calling him 'fasiq' or 'khabith') also leads to ta'zir, not hadd. Fourth, merely insulting without accusation (e.g., 'donkey', 'pig') does not even incur ta'zir (but may be subject to a judicial penalty). Finally, the limits of ta'zir are set: maximum 39 lashes, minimum 3 lashes. The proofs include sayings of tabi'un (al-Zuhri, Qatada, Ibrahim) and companions (Ali) supporting these distinctions. The Urdu commentary summarizes the principle: hadd requires the accused to be muhsan; otherwise, ta'zir applies. Thus, the rulings are consistent: slaves and non-Muslims are not muhsan, so their accusers receive ta'zir instead of hadd.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd penalty; its maximum in Hanafi school is 39 lashes, minimum 3.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; she is not free and thus not muhsan, so accusing her of zina does not incur hadd.
محصن (muhsan): A free, adult, chaste Muslim; the condition for receiving the hadd for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the maximum number of lashes for ta'zir in Hanafi fiqh?
A) 80 lashes
B) 39 lashes
C) 40 lashes
D) 10 lashes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the hadd for false accusation applies only if the accused is muhsan; otherwise, ta'zir (3-39 lashes) is imposed, and mere insults like 'donkey' incur no ta'zir.
